% \msCa\ 396.jpg
<TEXT> atikrodhena saudāsa atipānena yādavāḥ|</TEXT> 
        <APP>\vb <LEM>atipānena</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; atipāpena \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Saudāsa by excessive anger, the Yādavas by excessive drinking,</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Saudāsa, also known as Kalmāṣapāda, hit Śakti, Vasiṣṭha's son, with a whip because
                the latter did not give way to him, and as a consequence Śakti cursed Saudāsa:
                Saudāsa had to roam the world as a Rākṣasa for twelve years. 
                See Mahābhārata 1.166.1 ff.
                <sep/>
                As for the end of the Yādavas, see the short Mausalaparvan of the Mahābhārata (canto 16):
                cursed by the sages Viśvāmitra, Kaṇva and Nārada, and seeing menacing omens,
                the Yādavas take to drinking in Prabhāsa and destroy each other.
        </NOTE>
% check Saudāsa's death

<TEXT> atitṛṣṇāc{ }ca māndhātā nahuṣo dvijavajñayā||</TEXT> 4.57
<APP>\vc <LEM>atitṛṣṇāc{ }ca māndhātā</LEM> \conj;atitṛṣṇā ca māndāto \msCa,atitṛṣṇā ca māndhāto \msCb\msCc\msNa\msNc,atitṛṣṇā ca mandhāto \msNb,                atitṛṣṇā ca mānāc{ }ca ca \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>nahuṣo</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNc\Ed; naghuṣo \msNb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Māndhātṛ by excessive desire, Nahuṣa by contempt for Brahmins,</TR> -->
        <NOTE><sep/>Most probably, Łatitṛṣṇā$ in the MSS stand for Łatitṛṣṇāt$ (intending Łatitṛṣṇayā$).
                The form Łmāndhāto$ in \msCb\ stands for Łmāndhātā$ (nominative of Łmāndhātṛ$).
                I have corrected it in spite of the fact that the authors' knowledge about his story may
                come from Divyāvadāna 17, where it sometimes appears to be an a-stem noun (Łmāndāta$).
                Łdvijavajñayā$ in Łpāda$ d stands for Łdvijāvajñayā$ metri causa.
                <sep/>
                Māndhātṛ was born from his father's body who, being excessively thirsty once,
                had drank some decoction prepared for ritual purposes and as a result become pregnant with him.
                Nevertheless, Buddhacarita 11.13 suggests that Māndhātṛ himself was still unsatisfied
                with wordly objects even after he had obtained half of Indra's throne:
                <sep/>
                <skt>                devena vṛṣṭe 'pi hiraṇyavarṣe  <br/>
                                        dvīpān samagrāṃś caturo 'pi jitvā|  <br/>
                                     śakrasya cārdhāsanam apy avāpya   <br/>
                                        māndhātur āsīd viṣayeṣv atṛptiḥ||</skt> <sep/>
                In fact, as Monika Zin points out (2012: 149) Māndhātṛ/Māndhāta's rise and fall is a very popular theme
                in the `Narrative Art of the Amaravati School': 
                ``Statistics show that in the Amaravati School the most frequently represented narrative is
                  the story of King Māndhātar, which appears 47 times.''
        See ibid. p. 151:
        ''The story [e.g. <i>Divyāvadāna</i> XVII, see more sources in fn. 17 of this article] 
        relates that Māndhātar was a miraculously born <i>cakravartin</i> with Seven
        Jewels who could cause rain to fall so that his subjects could prosper; not usual rain, but rain
        of coins, of grain or of cloth. By virtue of his moral strength alone, Māndhātar conquered the world -
        without any weapons. He conquered all the countries on earth, then Uttarakuru,
        Pūrvavideha and Aparagodānīya, after which he set out to conquer the heavens. When he was
        traversing from one abode of the gods to the next (Nāgas, Sadāmattas, Mālādharas, etc.)
        groups of gods pledged obeisance to him and immediately marched in front of his troops.
        Māndhātar reached the splendid city of the Trayastriṃśa gods atop Sumeru, where Indra, in
        the meeting-hall, bequeathed to him half of his own seat and half of his heavenly realm.
        Māndhātar then ruled together with Indra for an unimaginable period of time during which 36
        Indras changed. One day, shortly after he won a battle against the Asuras, a sinful thought
        came to his mind: why should he rule alongside Indra? It was he, after all, who won the war,
        not Indra - he was better and should, therefore, rule alone.
        At that very moment Māndhatar fell from heaven, down to his former realm, became sick and died.
        Shortly before his death, he preached a sermon to his subjects in which <i>gātha</i>s 
        from the <i>Dhammapada</i> (186--187) appear...''
 
                <sep/>
                Nahuṣa was elevated to the position of Indra for a period of time and he also wanted
                to take Śacī, Indra's wife. Indra instructed Śacī to tell Nahuṣa to 
                harness some Ṛsis to a vehicle and use this vehicle to take Śacī. 
                Agastya, one of the Ṛṣis, was insulted even further by Nahuṣa, therefore
                he cursed Nahuṣa, who then fell from the vehicle. See Mahābhārata 12.329.35 ff. and
                the verse in the Buddhacarita (11.14) that follows the one about Māndhātṛ:
        <sep/>
                                <skt>        bhuktvāpi rājyaṃ divi devatānāṃ   <br/>
                                                śatakratau vṛtrabhayāt pranaṣṭe|<br/>
                                             darpān maharṣīn api vāhayitvā  <br/>
                                                kāmeṣv atṛpto nahuṣaḥ papāta||</skt>
                </NOTE>

Bibl:
Zin, Monika (2012). `Māndhātar, the Universal Monarch, and the Meaning of Representations of the Cakravartin in the Amaravati School, and of the Kings on the Kanaganahalli Stūpa.' In: Buddhist Narrative in Asia and Beyond: In Honour of HRH Princess Maha Chakri Sirindhorn. On Her Fifty-Fifth Birth Anniversary, Skilling, Peter / McDaniel, Justin (edd.) Bankok: Institute of Thai Studies, Chulalongkon University, vol. I



Buddhacarita:

samudravastrām api gām avāpya  
        pāraṃ jigīṣanti mahārṇavasya 
lokasya kāmair na vitṛptir asti  
         patadbhir ambhobhir ivārṇavasya  // 11.12 //

devena vṛṣṭe 'pi hiraṇyavarṣe  
        dvīpān (samagrāṃś C samudrāṃś ) caturo 'pi jitvā
śakrasya cārdhāsanam apy avāpya  
        *māndhātur* āsīd viṣayeṣv atṛptiḥ  // 11.13 //

bhuktvāpi rājyaṃ divi devatānāṃ   
        śatakratau vṛtrabhayāt pranaṣṭe
darpān maharṣīn api vāhayitvā  
        kāmeṣv atṛpto *nahuṣaḥ* papāta  // 11.14 //

aiḍaś ca rājā tridivaṃ vigāhya    [= Purūravas]
        nītvāpi devīṃ vaśam urvaśīṃ tām
lobhād ṛṣibhyaḥ kanakaṃ jihīrṣur  
        jagāma nāśaṃ viṣayeṣv atṛptaḥ  // 11.15 //

baler mahendraṃ nahuṣaṃ mahendrād   
        indraṃ punar ye nahuṣād upeyuḥ
svarge kṣitau vā viṣayeṣu teṣu  
        ko viśvased bhāgyakulākuleṣu  // 11.16 //
MBh 12:
Unto her Indra then said, Go and say
unto Nahusha that he should come to thee on a vehicle never used before,
viz., one unto which some Rishis should be harnessed, and arriving at
thine in that state he should wed thee. Indra has many kinds of vehicles
that are all beautiful and charming. All these have borne thee. Nahusha,
however, should come on such a vehicle that Indra himself had not
possessed. Thus counselled by her lord, Sachi left that spot with a
joyous heart. Indra also once more entered the fibres of that
lotus-stalk. Beholding the Queen of Indra come back to heaven, Nahusha
addressed her saying, The time thou hadst fixed is over. Unto him Sachi
said what Indra had directed her to say. *Harnessing a number of great
Rishis unto the vehicle he rode, Nahusha set out from his place for
coming to where Sachi was living.* The foremost of Rishis, viz., Agastya,
born within a jar, of the vital seed of Maitravaruna, beheld those
foremost of Rishis insulted by Nahusha in that way. Him Nahusha struck
with his foot. Unto him, Agastya said,--Wretch, as thou hast betaken
thyself to a highly improper act, do thou fall down on the Earth. Be
olong as the Earth and her hills continue. As soon as these words were
uttered by the great Rishi, Nahusha fell down from that vehicle. The
three worlds once more became master-less. The deities and the Rishis
then united together and proceeded to where Vishnu was and appealed to
him for bringing about the restoration of Indra. Approaching him, they
said,--O holy one, it behoveth thee to rescue Indra who is overwhelmed by
the sin of Brahmanicide. The boon-giving Vishnu replied unto them,
saying,--Let Sakra perform a Horse-sacrifice in honour of Vishnu. He will
then be restored to his former position. The deities and the Rishis began
to search for Indra, but when they could not find him, they went to Sachi
and said unto her,--O blessed lady, go unto Indra and bring him here.
transformed into a snake and do thou continue to live in that form as

<TEXT> atidyūtān{ }nalo rājā nṛgo goharaṇena tu||</TEXT> 4.58
        <APP>\vc <LEM>atidyūtān{ }nalo</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNb\msNc; atidyūtān{ }naro \msCb\msNa, atikhyātān{ }nalo \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>nṛgo go°</LEM> \Ed; nṛgaṅ{ }go° \msCa\msCc\msNb\msNc, nṛgaṃ go° \msCb\msNa</APP>
        <!-- <TR>King Nala by excessive gambling, Nṛga by taking a cow.</TR> -->
        <PARAL>\vo ŁAfter this verse, \Ed\ adds: $ 
                        tasmād{ }dama sadā sa rakṣet ati sarvatra varjayet
                       Ł(understand: $ tasmād{ }damaṃ sadā rakṣet ati sarvatra varjayetŁ)$</PARAL>
        %``Therefore one should always preserve Self-restraint and should always avoid excessiveness.''
               <NOTE><sep/> King Nala was an expert in the game of dice and lost his kingdom to Puṣkara in 
                            a game. See e.g. Mahābhārata 3.56.1 ff. 
                <sep/>
                       As for Nṛga, see Mahābhārata 14.93.74: <br/>
                       <skt>
                       gopradānasahasrāṇi dvijebhyo 'dān nṛgo nṛpaḥ|<br/>
                       ekāṃ dattvā sa pārakyāṃ narakaṃ samavāptavān||<br/>
                        
                       </skt>
                               (``King Nṛga had made gifts of thousands of cows for the twice-born.
                                 By giving away one single cow that belonged to someone else, 
                                 he fell into hell.'')
                </NOTE>

<APP>\va <LEM>hīnaḥ puruṣo dvijendra</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNc;                                hīna puruṣo dvijendra \msNb, hīnaṃ puruṣaṃ dvijendraḥ \Ed</APP>

% gender
<TEXT> svargaṃ ca mokṣaṃ ca sukhaṃ ca nāsti|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>there is no heaven, liberation or happiness.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Note how flexible the gender of most nouns is in pāda b: 
                        Łsvarga$, Łmokṣa$ and Łdama$ are usually masculine in standard Sanskrit.</NOTE>

% unmetr:
<TEXT> vijñānadharmakulakīrtināśa</TEXT> 
        <APP>\vc <LEM>°nāśa</LEM> \msCb; °nāśo \Ed °nāma \msCa\msCc\msNa, °naśca \msNb, °nāgā \msNc</APP>
        <NOTE>The majority of the witnesses suggest that pāda c ends in a stem form noun (Ł°nāśa$).
                This pāda is unmetrical, or rather it applies the licence of a word-final
                short syllable being counted as potentially long (Ł°dharMA°$). </NOTE>

% unmetr:
<TEXT> bhavanti vipra damayā vihīnāḥ||</TEXT> 4.59
<APP>\vd <LEM>vipra</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNaacorr\msNb\Ed; viprā \msNapcorr\msNc</APP>

        <!-- <TR>O Brahmin, people without Self-restraint 
                        are the destruction of knowledge, Dharma, family and fame.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Note how Łviprā$ in pāda d is probably an attempt in some MSS to restore the metre.
                This pāda is also unmetrical, or rather it applies the licence of a word-final
                short syllable being counted as potentially long (ŁviPRA$).</NOTE>

<SUBCHAPTER>yameṣu ghṛṇā (6)</SUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBCHAPTER>The sixth yama-rule: Taboos</TRSUBCHAPTER>

<TEXT> sūtake mṛtake śauṇḍe varṇabhraṣṭakule naṭe||</TEXT> 4.66
        <APP>\vc <LEM>śauṇḍe</LEM> \msNa; sauṇḍye \msCa\msCc\msNc, śoṇḍye \msCb, <UNCL>sauṇḍe</UNCL> \msNb, sauṇḍo \Ed</APP>
        <PARAL>\vo ŁThis verse is mostly illegible in \msNb$</PARAL>
        <!-- <TR>[e.g.] after birth or death [in the family], in case there are vendors of alcohol,
                in the case of a family having lost their caste, and in the case of a Naṭa [dancer caste?].</TR> -->
% kule ... bahuvrīhi individual
        <NOTE>One should probably understand Łśauṇḍe$ in pāda c as Łśauṇḍike$ (alternatively,
                it may be corrupted from Łṣaṇḍhe$); see both in Vāsiṣṭhadharmaśāstra 14.1--3:
                <sep/>
                <skt>athāto bhojyābhojyaṃ ca varṇayiṣyāmaḥ|
                cikitsaka-mṛgayu-puṃścalī-ḍaṇḍika-stenābhiśastar-ṣaṇḍha-patitānām annam abhojyam|
                kadarya-dīkṣita-baddhātura-somavikrayi-takṣa-rajaka-śauṇḍika-sūcaka-vārdhuṣika-carmāvakṛntānām||</skt> etc.
                <sep/>
                In Olivelle's translation (DhSūtras 1999: 285):
                        ``Next we will describe food that is fit and food that is
                        unfit to be eaten [...] The following are unfit
                        to be eaten: food given by a physician, a hunter, a harlot, a law
                        enforcement agent, a thief, a heinous sinner [...] a
                        eunuch, or an outcaste; as also that given by a miser, a man
                        consecrated for a sacrifice, a prisoner, a sick person, a man who
                        sells Soma, a carpenter, a washerman, a liquor dealer, a spy, an
                        usurer, a leather worker...''
                <sep/>
                In support of reading Łṣaṇḍhe$, see Manu 3.239:
                <sep/>
                        <skt>cāṇḍālaś ca varāhaś ca kukkuṭaḥ śvā tathaiva ca|<br/>
                        rajasvalā ca ṣaṇḍhaś ca nekṣerann aśnato dvijān||</skt></NOTE>
% check sauṇḍa as a jāti ṣaṇḍha ! Judit but also śuṇḍa -- śauṇḍa : connected to bar more likely
% notable examples

        <!-- <TR>Compassion, sympathy in joy, indifference, and benevolence are the four sanctuaries/planes.</TR> -->

                could this use of the term Łāyatana$ for the four Buddhist 
                Łbrahmavihāra$s have been influenced by the following passage in the Dharmasamuccaya (date?)?
        <sep/>
                        <skt>mokṣasyāyatanāni ṣaṭ|<br/>
                        apramādas tathā śraddhā vīryārambhas tathā dhṛtiḥ|<br/>
                        jñānābhyāsaḥ saṃtāśleṣo mokṣasyāyatanāni ṣaṭ||1.3||<br/>
                        nava śāntisamprāptihetavaḥ|</br>
                        dānaṃ śīlaṃ damaḥ kṣāntir maitrī bhūteṣv ahiṃsatā|<br/>
                        karuṇāmuditopekṣā śāntisamprāptihetavaḥ||1.4||<br/></skt>
</NOTE>

<SUBCHAPTER>yameṣu mādhuryam (9)</SUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBCHAPTER>The ninth yama-rule: Charm</TRSUBCHAPTER>

% Törzsök
<TEXT> kāyavāṅmanamādhuryaṃ cakṣur{ }buddhiś{ }ca pañcamaḥ|</TEXT>
<APP>\vab <LEM>manamādhuryaṃ ca°</LEM> \eme; °manasā dhūryaś{ }ca° \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNc,°mana<UNCL>mā</UNCL>dhūryaś{ }ca° \msCb,                                                       °mana¤dhūrya¤° \msNb, °manasā bhūyaś{ }ca° \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°kṣur{ }buddhi°</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNc\Ed; °kṣu buddhi° \msCc\msNa, ¤¤¤ \msNb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>[Charm has five types:] bodily, verbal and mental charm, 
                        [charm of] the eyes and [of one's] thoughts pañcamaḥ.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>My emendation from Ł°manasā dhūryaś$ to Ł°mana-mādhuryaś$ is based on the fact that following the list
                of Łyama$s in 3.16cd--17ab, we need some reference to Łmādhurya$ here and that it is easy to see how this
                 corruption came about: Ł°mano-mādhurya°$ would be unmetrical, thus the form Ł°mana-mādhurya$;
                        Ł°mana-mā°$ is easily corrupted to Ł°manasā°$ (not to mention the fact 
                        that Łmanasā$ comes up in the next verse); 
                        in addition we need five items in this line because of Łpañcamaḥ$.
                        As always, I correct Łmādhūrya$ to Łmādhurya$, although it seems that 
                        the former is acceptable in this text. 
                        I did not correct Łmādhuryaś$ to Łmādhuryaṃ$ because of the corresponding
                        Łpañcamaḥ$.</NOTE>

<TEXT> saumyadṛṣṭipradānaṃ ca krūrabuddhiṃ ca varjayet||</TEXT> 4.83
        <APP>\vc <LEM>°dānaṃ ca</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNc; ¤¤ \msNb, °dānaś{ }ca \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>°buddhiṃ ca</LEM> \msCa\msNa\msNc; buddhiś{ }ca \msCb, °dṛṣṭiṃ ca \msCc\Ed, ¤¤¤ \msNb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Giving [others] a friendly glance [is commendable] and one should avoid cruel thoughts.</TR> -->

<TEXT> prasannamanasā dhyāyet{ }priyavākyam{ }udīrayet|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>prasanna°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\Ed; <UNCL>prasanna</UNCL>° \msNb, prasaṃna° \msNc</APP>
        <!-- <TR>One should meditate with a tranquil mind and should speak [to other people using] gentle words.</TR> -->

<TEXT> iti yamapravibhāgaḥ kīrtito 'yaṃ dvijendra</TEXT>
<APP>\va <LEM>yamapravibhāgaḥ</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNb\msNc; yamavibhāgaḥ \msCc,yamapraribhāgaḥ \msNa, niyamaparibhāgaḥ \Ed</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>dvijendra</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; narendra \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Thus has been taught this section on the Łyama$-rules, O great Brahmin.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>In pāda a Ł°pra°$ does not make the previous syllable long: this is the phenomenon of
                `muta cum liquida', one of the hallmarks of the ŁVṛṣasārasaṃgraha$, 
                that is, syllables such as Łtra, pra, bra, dra$ do not necessarily make the 
                previous syllable long.</NOTE>

%                                       taṃ? tat in \msCc
<TEXT> iha parata sukhārthaṃ kārayet{ }taṃ manuṣyaḥ|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°yet{ }taṃ manuṣyaḥ</LEM> \corr; °yet{ }tan{ }manuṣyaḥ °yet{ }tat{ }manuṣyaḥ \msCc</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Humans should follow them to reach happiness here and in the other world.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>In pāda b, Łparata$ most probably stands for Łparatra$ or Łparataḥ$ metri causa. 
        We may correct it to Łparatra$ (`muta cum liquida').</NOTE>

<TEXT> duritamalapahārī śaṅkarasyājñayāste</TEXT>
<APP>\vc <LEM>durita°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; irita° \Ed</APP>
<APP><LEM>°pahārī</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; °palapahārī \msCc</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>°jñayāste</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNb\msNc\Ed; °jñayāte \msNa</APP>
        <!-- <TR>He'll live by Śaṅkara's command with his filth of sins destroyed.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Ł°malapahārī$ in the MSS stands either for Ł°malāpahārī$ or Ł°malaprahārī$ metri causa. 
                I could have choosen to emend it to Ł°malaprahārī$ (`muta cum liquida' again),
                but I decided not to because Łapahārin$, Łapahāra$
                Łapahāraka$ are used in the text very frequently. See also 8.XX, which contains a very similar expression:
                        Łsakalamalapahāre dharmapañcāśad etat$.</NOTE>

         % should it not be cchatra? unmetr...  eme: pravartā (pravartṛ)
% cakravartā 
% ekāṭapattra Nirajan like my pravṛtṛ
<TEXT> bhavati pṛthivibhartā hy{ }ekachatrapravartā||</TEXT> 4.89
        <APP>\vd <LEM>°vartā</LEM> \conj; °vṛttā \mssCaCbCc\msNb\msNc, °vṛttāḥ \msNa\Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>He'll become a ruler of the world [that he subjugates] under one royal umbrella.</TR> -->
% एकातपत्रं जगतः

<SUBSUBCHAPTER>āhāraśaucam</SUBSUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>Purity of the food</TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>
%5.10  ma-vipulā
<TEXT> āhāraśaucaṃ vakṣyāmi śṛṇuṣvāvahito bhava|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>I shall teach you the rules of purity with food. Listen, pay great attention.</TR> -->
        <APP>\vb <LEM>śṛṇuṣvāvahito</LEM> \msCb\msCc\msNa\msNc\Ed; śṛṇu<UNCL>ṣvāva</UNCL>¤¤ \msCa, śṛṇuṣvavahito \msNb</APP>

%\msCa\ 399.jpg
<TEXT> bhāgadvayaṃ tu bhuñjīta bhāgam{ }ekaṃ jalaṃ pibet|</TEXT> 
        <APP>\vd <LEM>pibet</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; pibe \msCb</APP>

%               EMEND?
<TEXT> vāyusaṃcāradānārthaṃ caturtham{ }avaśeṣayet||</TEXT> 5.10
        <APP>\ve <LEM>°cāradānārthaṃ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; °cāraṇārthāya \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>He should eat [as much] food [that fills] two quarters [of the stomach] and drink water [that fills] one quarter.
                 In order to be able to practise breath-control, he should save the remaining quarter.</TR> -->
                % pāda d iambic?
        <NOTE>\vo For similar instructions, see a verse cited in Śaṅkara's commentary ad BhG 6.16:
                                Łuktaṃ hi| 
                                ardhaṃ savyañjanānnasya tṛtīyam{ }udakasya ca| 
                                vāyoḥ saṃcaraṇārthaṃ tu caturtham{ }avaśeṣayet||$
                               (``Half is for food with sauce, the third part for water,
                               but in order to be able to move the air, he should leave the fourth part [empty].'')
                See also e.g. Aṣṭāṅgahṛdaya 8.46cd-47ab:
                                        Łannena kukṣer dvāv aṃśau pānenaikaṃ prapūrayet|| 
                                        āśrayaṃ pavanādīnāṃ caturtham avaśeṣayet|$
                and Sannyāsopaniṣad 59: 
                                        Łāhārasya ca bhāgau dvau tṛtīyam udakasya ca| 
                                        vāyoḥ saṃcaraṇārthāya caturtham avaśeṣayet||$ </NOTE>

<TEXT> snigdhasvādurasaiḥ ṣaḍbhir{ }āhāraṣaḍrasair{ }budhaḥ|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>°svādu°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNc; °svā¤ \msNb, °svāda° \Ed</APP>
<APP>\vb <LEM>°ṣaḍrasair{ }bu°</LEM> \msCb\Ed; °sadravair{ }bu° \msCa\msNa\msNc,                                        °sadravai bu° \msCc, °ṣaḍrasai bu° \msNb</APP>

<TEXT> dhātuvaiṣamyanāśo 'sti na ca rogāḥ sudāruṇāḥ||</TEXT> 5.11
% vaiśamya \msCa\msCc, daiśamya? \msCb
<APP>\vc <LEM>°vaiṣamyanāśo 'sti</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc;                      °<UNCL>dai</UNCL>ṣamyanāśāsti \msCb, °vaiṣamya naśyanti \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>sudāruṇāḥ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; sudāruṇaḥ \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>[By] the wise one['s applying] the six soft and sweet juices, [which are] the six juices in food,
                the disturbances of the Łdhātu$s and the terrible illnesses will disappear.</TR> -->

% Olivelle: Manu p.340 note to Manu 11.57 abhakṣya is forbidden, abhojya is unfit food
<TEXT> abhakṣyaṃ ca na bhakṣeta apeyaṃ na ca pāyayet|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>abhakṣyaṃ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNc; ¤¤¤ \msNb, abhakṣaṃ \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>na ca</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb; ca na \msNc\Ed</APP>

<TEXT> agamyaṃ na ca gamyeta avācyaṃ na ca bhāṣayet||</TEXT> 5.12
        <APP>\vd <LEM>avācyaṃ</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; avācaṃ \msCc</APP>
        <!-- <TR>He should not eat foods that are forbidden and he should not drink drinks that are forbidden.
                 He should not go where he is not allowed to and he should not say what is improper.</TR> -->

<TEXT> laśunaṃ ca palāṇḍuṃ ca gṛñjanaṃ kacakāni ca|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>palāṇḍuṃ</LEM> \Ed; palaṇḍuṃ \mssCaCbCc\msNb\msNc, palaḍuṃ \msNa</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>kavakāni</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; ca kacāni \Ed</APP>

                gain happiness at the end of time, eternally embellished with glory and fame.
                He has reached here in this world all the merits that the books on true Dharma teach, 
        i       and at the end of his life he will undoubtedly reach the desired path in the other world.</TR> -->

                and the sandhi-bridge Ł-m-$ in Łparatra-m-īhita°$. </NOTE>

<TEXT> yenedaṃ tapa tapyate sumanasā saṃsāraduḥkhacchidam</TEXT>
<APP>\va <LEM>tapa ta°</LEM> \Ed; tapas{ }ta° \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\ \unmetr</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>°manasā</LEM> \eme; °manasaḥ \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed</APP>

% stem form
%      - - - .  . -  .  -  . . . -      -   -  . -     -    . -
<TEXT> āśāpāśa vimucya nirmalamatis{ }tyaktvā jaghanyaṃ phalam|</TEXT>
<APP>\vb <LEM>nirmalamati°</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; nirmalarmati° \msCb</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>jaghanyaṃ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; jagat{ }yaṃ \Ed</APP>

<TEXT> svargākāṅkṣyanṛpatvabhogaviṣayaṃ sarvāntikaṃ tat{ }phalam</TEXT>
<APP>\vc <LEM>°kāṅkṣya°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; °kāṃkṣa° \Ed</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>sarvāntikaṃ</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; sarvārttikaṃ \msCb</APP>

<TEXT> jantuḥ śāśvatajanmamṛtyubhavane tanniṣṭhasādhyaṃ vahet||</TEXT> 6.29
<APP>\vd <LEM>°bhavane</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\Ed; °bhavene \msNc</APP>
<APP><LEM>°sādhyaṃ vahet</LEM> \msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; °<UNCL>sādhyam</UNCL>¤¤ \msCa,                                                  °sādhya vahet \msCb, °sādhyaṃ vadet \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>A person who performs with a well-disposed mind 
                this penance that puts an end to the suffering caused by mundane existence,
                abandoning the trap of hope, with a spotless mind, giving up the lowest rewards
                [such as] wishing for heaven, being a king and having enjoyments for the senses,
                can bring that ultimate [? Łsarvāntika$] reward which stems from it [i.e. from Łtapas$]  
                to [this] home of eternal births and deaths.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Note the stem form Ł°pāśa$ in Łpāda$ b metri causa.</NOTE>

<SUBCHAPTER>niyameṣu dānam (4)</SUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBCHAPTER>The fourth niyama-rule: Donation</TRSUBCHAPTER>

% tathaivāhuḥ?
<TEXT> dānāni ca tathety{ }āhuḥ pañcadhā munibhiḥ purā|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>tathety{ }āhuḥ</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNb\msNc\Ed; tathaity{ }āhuḥ \msCb\msNa</APP>
        <!-- <TR>In the past the wise declared that there were five kinds of donation ... CHECK</TR> -->

% stem form dāna?
<TEXT> annaṃ vastraṃ hiraṇyaṃ ca bhūmi godāna pañcamam||</TEXT> 7.1
        <APP>\vc <LEM>vastraṃ</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNc\Ed; vastra \msCc\msNb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Donation of food, clothes, gold, land and the fifth, donation of cows.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Łtathety$ is suspicious. Note how Łannaṃ$, Łvastraṃ$, Łhiraṇyaṃ$ and Łbhūmi$ (the latter treated as neuter, or given in
                                stem form) are all meant to go with -Łdāna$ (again, in stem form, metri causa).</NOTE>

        <!-- <TR>From food [comes] energy, memory, the vital breath, growth, body, happiness.</TR> -->

        <APP>\va <LEM>annāj{ }jī°</LEM> \msCa\msNa\msNb\Ed; annā jī° \msCb\msCc\msNc</APP>

        <!-- <TR>Living beings live on food. Food always satisfies.</TR> -->

        <!-- <TR>From food arise desire, rapture, pride and valour.</TR> -->

        <APP>\vab <LEM>°vyādhīn{ }sa°</LEM> \msCb\msNc; °vyādhān{ }sa° \msCa\msCc\msNb, °vādhān{ }sa° \msNa, °vyādhā sa° \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>vināśayet</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; viśayet \msCb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Food drives away hunger and thirst and disease instantly.</TR> -->

<TEXT> annadānāc{ }ca saubhāgyaṃ khyātiḥ kīrtiś{ }ca jāyate||</TEXT> 7.4
        <!-- <TR>From donations of food arise happiness, fame and glory.</TR> -->

<TEXT> annadaḥ prāṇadaś{ }caiva prāṇadaś{ }cāpi sarvadaḥ|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>annadaḥ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; annada \Ed</APP>

<APP>                 <LEM>sarvadaḥ</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; sarvadāḥ \msCc</APP>
        <!-- <TR>He who donates food donates life. He who donates life donates everything.</TR> -->

% \msNa\ 204.jpg lower, f.11r

        <APP>\vd <LEM>bhūtaṃ</LEM> \msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; ×tan \msCa, bhūte \msCb, bhūto \Ed</APP>
        <PARAL>\vcd Ł \kb\ MBh 13.62.6ab: $annena sadṛśaṃ dānaṃ na bhūtaṃ na bhaviṣyati</PARAL>
        <!-- <TR>Therefore nothing is equal to the donation of food, nothing was, nothing will be.</TR> -->




<SUBSUBCHAPTER>vastradānam</SUBSUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>Donation of clothes</TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>

%                               means śriyam api? kriyām api?
<TEXT> vastrābhāvān{ }manuṣyasya śriyād{ }api parityajet|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>°bhāvān{ }ma°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNb\Ed; °bhāvāt{ }ma° \msNa\msNc</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>śriyād{ }api</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\Ed; priyād{ }api \msCb, śriyā vāpi \msNc</APP>
        <!-- <TR>...  ? </TR> -->
                        Brahmapurāṇa: 
                         vastrābhāve kriyā nāsti yajñā vedās tapāṃsi ca |
                         tasmād vāsāṃsi deyāni śrāddhakāle viśeṣataḥ ||220.139|


<TEXT> vastrahīno na pūjyeta bhāryāputrasakhādibhiḥ||</TEXT> 7.6
        <!-- <TR>A person without clothes may not be respected by his wife, son, friends etc.</TR> -->

<TEXT> vidyāvān{ }sukulīno 'pi jñānavān{ }guṇavān{ }api|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>Be it a learned person from a good family or an intelligent and virtuous one,</TR> -->

<TEXT> vastrahīnaḥ parādhīnaḥ paribhūtaḥ pade pade||</TEXT> 7.7
        <!-- <TR>a person without clothes is subdued and humiliated on every occasion</TR> -->

<TEXT> apamānam{ }avajñāṃ ca vastrahīno hy{ }avāpnuyāt|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>°vajñāṃ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; °vajñaṃ \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°hīno</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; °hī \msCb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>because a person without clothes receives contempt and disrespect.</TR> -->

<TEXT> jugupsati mahātmāpi sabhāstrījanasaṃsadi||</TEXT> 7.8
        <!-- <TR>Even a great soul will try to avoid [him] at the court, among women, in an assembly.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>The intention originally may have been this: ``Even if he is a great soul, he will be avoided...''</NOTE>

<TEXT> tasmād{ }vastrapradānāni praśaṃsanti manīṣiṇaḥ|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>Therefore the wise praise donations of clothes.</TR> -->

%Naraharinatha p.602
<TEXT> na jīrṇaṃ sphuṭitaṃ dadyād{ }vastraṃ kutsitam{ }eva vā||</TEXT> 7.9
        <APP>\vc <LEM>jīrṇaṃ sphuṭitaṃ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNc; jīrṇasphaṭitaṃ \msNb\Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>kutsitam{ }eva vā</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb\Ed; kutsitam{ }eva ca \msCc, kutsitmeva vā \msNc</APP>
        <!-- <TR>One should not give away old, torn or dirty clothes.</TR> -->

<TEXT> navaṃ purāṇarahitaṃ mṛdu sūkṣmaṃ suśobhanam|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>sūkṣmaṃ</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc; sūkṣma \msCc, śuklaṃ \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>[Clothes] should be donated [only if they are] new, not worn,
                 soft, delicate and beautiful,</TR> -->

<TEXT> susaṃskṛtya pradātavyaṃ śraddhābhaktisamanvitam||</TEXT> 7.10
        <APP>\vc <LEM>°dātavyaṃ</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; °dātavya \msCc</APP>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>°samanvitam</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNapcorr\msNb\msNc\Ed; °taṃ \msNaacorr</APP>
        <!-- <TR>well-washed, and [if] accompanied by willingness and devotion.</TR> -->

<TEXT> śraddhāsattvaviśeṣeṇa deśakālavidhena ca|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>°sattva°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; °sa ca° \Ed</APP>

<TEXT> pātradravyaviśeṣeṇa phalam{ }āhuḥ pṛthak{ }pṛthak||</TEXT> 7.11
        <PARAL>\vo Łcf. Manu 7.86--87 (the latter usually labelled as an additional verse): $
                        pātrasya hi viśeṣeṇa śraddadhānatayāiva ca| 
                        alpaṃ vā bahu vā pretya dānasya phalam{ }aśnute||
                        deśakālavidhānena dravyaṃ śraddhāsamanvitam|
                        pātre pradīyate yat{ }tu tad{ }dharmasya prasādhanam||</PARAL>
        <!-- <TR>They say that the reward [of donation/generosity] is in every case dependent on the
                particular [donor's] willingness and character, the choice of place and time, and on
                the particular recipient and material.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>It seems that Łvidhena ca$ stands for Łvidhinā ca$ or rather Łvidhānena$ metri causa in Łpāda$ b.</NOTE>

<TEXT> yādṛśaṃ dīyate vastraṃ tādṛśaṃ prāpyate phalam|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>The reward received will be similar to the clothes donated.</TR> -->

<TEXT> jīrṇavastrapradānena jīrṇavastram{ }avāpnuyāt|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>By donating old clothes, one would receive old clothes [as a reward].</TR> -->

<TEXT> śobhanaṃ dīyate vastraṃ śobhanaṃ vastram{ }āpnuyāt||</TEXT> 7.12
        <!-- <TR>By donating beautiful clothes, one would receive beautiful clothes [as a reward].</TR> -->


<NOTANUSTUBH/> śārdūlavikrīḍita 
% stem form
% \msNb\ 52.jpg upper
%       -  -     -   .  . -  . -    . . . -  - -  .  -   - . -
<TEXT> dadyād{ }vastra suśobhanaṃ dvijavare kāle śubhe sādaram</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>dvijavare kāle śubhe</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; dvijayine ekāśubhaṃ \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Should one bestow very beautiful clothes on a Brahmin [lit. on a person who is first among the twice-born] 
                        in an auspicious time, respectfully.</TR> -->

% unmetr:
<TEXT> saubhāgyam{ }atulaṃ labheta sa naro rūpaṃ tathā śobhanam|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>naro</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; daro \msCb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>he [i.e. the donor] will receive unequalled happiness and a beautiful appearance.</TR> -->

% stem form
<TEXT> tasmin{ }yāti suvastrakoṭi śataśaḥ prāpnoti niḥsaṃśayam</TEXT>
<APP>\vc <LEM>tasmin{ }yāti</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNb\msNc\Ed; ta<UNCL>smā</UNCL>n{ }yāti \msNa</APP>
<APP><LEM>suvastra°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; sa vastra° \Ed</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>°saṃśayam</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNc; °saṃśayaḥ \msCc\msNa\msNb\Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>When he departs, he will be given hundreds of millions of items of nice clothes, no doubt about that.</TR> -->

<TEXT> tasmāt{ }tvaṃ kuru vastradānam{ }asakṛt{ }pāratrikotkarṣaṇam||</TEXT> 7.13
        <APP>\vd <LEM>dānam{ }asakṛt{ }pā°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNc\Ed; dānasat{ }pā° \msNb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Therefore do donate clothes often. It is the way up to the other world.</TR> -->




<SUBSUBCHAPTER>suvarṇadānam</SUBSUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>Donation of gold</TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>
<ANUSTUBH/>
% stem form or ma-vipulā
<TEXT> suvarṇadānaṃ viprendra saṃkṣipya kathayāmy{ }aham|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>°dānaṃ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNc; °dāna \msNb\Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>O great Brahmin, now I shall teach you about the donation of gold in a concise manner.</TR> -->

<TEXT> pavitraṃ maṅgalaṃ puṇyaṃ sarvapātakanāśanam||</TEXT> 7.14
        <APP>\vd <LEM>°pātaka°</LEM>  \msCb\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; °pāpaka° \msCa</APP>
        <!-- <TR>It is pure, auspicious and meritorious [act] and it washes off all sins.</TR> -->

% \msCc\ 203.jpg, f.280r
<TEXT> dhārayet{ }satataṃ vipra suvarṇakaṭakāṅgulim|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°kaṭakāṅgulim</LEM> \msCb\msCc\msNa\msNc\Ed; °ka¤¤gulim \msCa, °kaṭakāṅgulam \msNb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Should one hand over [to someone] a golden bracelet or ring, O Brahmin,</TR> -->
        <NOTE>I suspect that Łaṅguli$ is used here in the sense of Łaṅgulīya$ (`finger-ring').</NOTE>

<TEXT> mucyate sarvapāpebhyo rāhunā candramā yathā||</TEXT> 7.15
        <!-- <TR>he will be freed of all sins, just as the moon is freed from [the demon] Rāhu.</TR> -->
        <PARAL>\vcd Ł = 22.38 CHECK $</PARAL>

% ma-vipulā:
<TEXT> dattvā suvarṇaṃ viprebhyo devebhyaś{ }ca dvijarṣabha|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>suvarṇaṃ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNc\Ed; suvarṇa \msNb</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°rṣabha</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNc\Ed; °rṣabhaḥ \msCc\msNb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>If a person donates  gold to Brahmins or gods, O excellent Brahmin,</TR> -->

<TEXT> tuṭimātre 'pi yo dadyāt{ }sarvapāpaiḥ pramucyate||</TEXT> 7.16
<APP>\vc <LEM>tuṭi°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; truṭi° \Ed</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>°mātre</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNb\msNc; °mātro \msNa\Ed</APP>
<APP>\vd <LEM>sarvapāpaiḥ pramucyate</LEM> \msCb\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc;                                 sarvapāpaiḥ sa mucyate \msCa, sarvapāpai pramucyate \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>even if it is only in a minute quantity, he will be freed of all sins.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>The form Łtuṭi$ as a widespread variant of Łtuṭi$, see e.g. CHECK.</NOTE>

% units of measure:
<TEXT> raktimāṣakakarṣaṃ vā palārdhaṃ palam{ }eva vā|</TEXT>
<APP>\va <LEM>raktimāṣaka°</LEM> \msNcacorr; rantimāṣaka° \msCa, rattimāṣaka° \msCb\msNa\msNcpcorr,                                                        rantimmānsaka° \msCc, rattimānsaka° \msNb, rattimāṣaka° \Ed </APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°rdhaṃ</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNc\Ed; °ddha \msCc\msNa\msNb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>[The amount can be just] one Łrakti$, a Łmāṣaka$, a Łkarṣa$, half a Łpala$ or a Łpala$:</TR> -->
% raktikā  f. Abrus Precatorius (its seed or grain is used as a weight = 1/6, 1/7, or 2/15 Māṣaka), ŚārṅgS.
% karṣa  mn. a weight of gold or silver (= 16 Māṣas = 80 Rettis = 1/4 Pala = 1/400 of a Tulā = about 176 grains troy
 in common use 8 Rettis are given to the Māṣa, and the Karṣa is then about 280 grains troy), Suśr.


<TEXT> evam{ }eva phalaṃ vṛddhir{ }jñeyā dānaviśeṣataḥ||</TEXT> 7.17
        <APP>\vcd <LEM>vṛddhir{ }jñeyā</LEM> \msCa\Ed; vṛddhi jñeyā \msCb\msCc\msNa\msNb, vṛrddhi jñeyā \msNc</APP>
        <!-- <TR>this is exactly how the increase in the [size of the corresponding] reward will be, 
                                in proportion to the kind [i.e.\ amount] of the donation.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>I suspect that Łphalaṃ vṛddhir$ stands for Łphalavṛddhir$ (Łphalasya vṛddhiḥ$) metri causa, meaning
                                `the increase of the reward'.</NOTE>





<SUBSUBCHAPTER>bhūmidānam</SUBSUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>Donation of land</TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>

<TEXT> sarvādhāraṃ mahīdānaṃ praśaṃsanti manīṣiṇaḥ|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>°dhāraṃ</LEM> \msCb; °dhāra° \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vab <LEM>°dānaṃ praśaṃsanti</LEM> \msCb\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; dā¤<UNCL>nam{ }pra</UNCL>×santi \msCa</APP>
        <!-- <TR>The wise praise the donation of land as the basis of everything [else].</TR> -->

% \msCa\ 403.jpg, f.204r
<TEXT> annavastrahiraṇyādi sarvaṃ vai bhūmisambhavam||</TEXT> 7.18
        <APP>\vd <LEM>sarvaṃ vai</LEM> \msCb\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; sarvaṃ <UNCL>ve</UNCL> \msCa\ \toplost</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Food, clothes, gold etc.: all of these originate in the land.</TR> -->

% \msNc\ 222.jpg upper
<TEXT> bhūmidānena viprendra sarvadānaphalaṃ labhet|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°phalaṃ labhet</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\Ed; °lalaṃ bhavet \msNcacorr, °laṃ bhavet \msNc</APP>
        <!-- <TR>O Brahmin, one can obtain all the rewards of donation be donating land.</TR> -->

<TEXT> bhūmidānasamaṃ vipra yady{ }asti vada tattvataḥ||</TEXT> 7.19
        <!-- <TR>If there is anything that equals the donation of land, O Brahmin, you should really tell me.</TR> -->

<TEXT> mātṛkukṣivimuktas{ }tu dharaṇīśaraṇo bhavet|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>°muktas{ }tu</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; °muktis{ }tu \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°śaraṇo</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb; °śaraṇa \msNc, °śaraṇāṃ \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>[Humans] have the earth as their abode as soon as they get out of their mother's womb.</TR> -->

<TEXT> carācarāṇāṃ sarveṣāṃ bhūmiḥ sādhāraṇā smṛtā||</TEXT> 7.20
        <!-- <TR>Land is taught as common to all that is mobile and immobile.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>I take Łsādhāraṇā$ as one word, but it is possible that the intention of the author
                        was Łsā dhāraṇā$ in two words, in fact meaning Łsādhāraḥ$ (Łsā ādhāraḥ$, `it is the basis').</NOTE>

<TEXT> ekahastaṃ dvihastaṃ vā pañcāśac{ }chatam{ }eva vā|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>ekahastaṃ</LEM> \msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc; ekahasta° \msCa\msCc\Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Be it [only a land of] one forearm, two forearms, fifty or a hundred,</TR> -->

% \msNa\ 205.jpg upper, f.11v
<TEXT> sahasrāyutalakṣaṃ vā bhūmidānaṃ praśasyate||</TEXT> 7.21
<APP>\vd <LEM>bhūmidānaṃ praśasyate</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNc\Ed; bhūmidāna praśasyate \msCb,                        pañcāśac{ }chatam{ }eva vā| sahāyutalakṣam{ }vā bhūmidaṃ praśasyate \msNb\ Ł(eyeskip)$</APP>
        <!-- <TR>a thousand, ten thousand, a hundred thousand, donations of land are held in great esteem.</TR> -->

% \msCb\ 422.jpg, f.210v
<TEXT> ekahastāṃ ca yo bhūmiṃ dadyād{ }dvijavarāya tu|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>°hastāṃ ca</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNc\Ed; °hastañ{ }ca \msCb\msNb</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>dadyād{ }dvi°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; dadyā dvi° \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Should he donate a piece of land of [only] one forearm to an excellent Brahmin,</TR> -->

<TEXT> varṣakoṭiśataṃ divyaṃ svargaloke mahīyate||</TEXT> 7.22
        <!-- <TR>he will enjoy a billion divine years in heaven.</TR> -->

<TEXT> evaṃ bahuṣu hasteṣu guṇāguṇi phalaṃ smṛtam|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>guṇāguṇi°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; guṇāgaṇi° \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Thus in case of many forearms [of land], the reward is said to be 
                        [proportional to the dimensions of the land, i.e.] ...  </TR> -->

<TEXT> śraddhādhikaṃ phalaṃ dānaṃ kathitaṃ te dvijottama||</TEXT> 7.23
        <APP>\vc <LEM>°dhikaṃ</LEM> \msCb\msCc\msNa\msNb; °dhika° \msCa\msNc\Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>°ttama</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\Ed; °ttamaḥ \msNc</APP>
        <!-- <TR>O Brahmin, I have taught you about the rewards of donation that is made willingly.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>I think that Łguṇāguṇi$, or perhaps Łguṇaguṇi$ (which would be unmetrical), should refer to the idea
                        that e.g. the donation of a piece of land of 2 x 2 Łhasta$s would result in 
                        4 x Łkoṭiśata$ years in heaven, Łguṇa$ generally meaning `times'. But this is only a guess, and
                        it needs to be supported by some similar passage.
                        I suspect that Łpāda$ c is an awkward attempt at saying Łśraddhādhikadāna(sya) phalaṃ$.</NOTE>

% rāmena \msCc\msNa\msNb
<TEXT> jāmadagnyena rāmeṇa bhūmiṃ dattvā dvijāya vai|</TEXT>
<APP>\va <LEM>jāmadagnyena</LEM> \msCb\msNa\msNc; jāmadagnye¤ \msCa, jāmadagnena \msCc\msNb\Ed</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>rāmeṇa</LEM> \msCb\msNc\Ed; rāmena \msCc\msNa\msNb, ¤¤ṇa \msCa</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>dattvā dvi°</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; dadyād{ }dvi° \msCb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>[Paraśu]rāma, the son of Jamadagni, having donated land to the Brahmin [Kaśyapa],</TR> -->
        <NOTE>See entry `Paraśurāma' in Purāṇic Enc.:
                <sep/>
                                To atone for the sin of slaughtering even
                                innocent Kṣatriyas, Paraśurāma gave away all his
                                riches as gifts to brahmins. He invited all the brahmins
                                to Samantapañcaka and conducted a great Yāga there.
                                The chief Ṛtvik (officiating priest) of the Yāga was
                                the sage Kaśyapa and Paraśurāma gave all the lands
                                he conquered till that time to Kaśyapa. Then a plat-
                                form of gold ten yards long and nine yards wide was
                                made and Kaśyapa was installed there and worshipped.
                                After the worship was over according to the instructions
                                from Kaśyapa the gold platform was cut into pieces
                                and the gold pieces were offered to brahmins.
                                When Kaśyapa got all the lands from Paraśurāma he
                                said thus:—“Oh Rāma, you have given me all your
                                land and it is not now proper for you to live in my
                                soil. You can go to the south and live somewhere on
                                the shores of the ocean there.” Paraśurāma walked
                                south and requested the ocean to give him some land to
                                live. </NOTE>

        <!-- <TR>obtained eternal life in this very world, O excellent Brahmin.</TR> -->

<TEXT> dānād{ }eva ca śakralokasakalaṃ dānāj{ }janānandanam</TEXT>
<APP>\va <LEM>śakralokasakalaṃ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNb\msNc; śatrulokasakalaṃ \msNa, śakralokam{ }atulaṃ \Ed</APP>

                                Donations make people happy.</TR> -->

<TEXT> dānād{ }eva mahīṃ samasta bubhuje samrāḍ{ }mahīmaṇḍale|</TEXT>
<APP>\vb <LEM>dānād{ }eva</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; dāned{ }eva \msCb</APP>
<APP><LEM>mahīṃ samasta</LEM> \conj; mahīsamāsu \msCb\msCc, mahīṃ samāṃsu \msCa\msNa\msNc,mahī samasta \msNb, mahīyasāṃ sa \Ed</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>samrāḍ{ }ma°</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; saṃmrāḍ{ }ma° \msCb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Samrāj enjoyed the whole earth in the world only because of donations. CHECK </TR> -->
        <NOTE>Revise.</NOTE>
Purāṇic Enc.:
SAMRĀṬ . The grand-daughter of Manu Svāyambhuva
and the daughter of Priyavrata, who had married the
daughter of Kardama. Ten sons and two daughters
named Samrāṭ and Kukṣi were born to Priyavrata.
(Viṣṇu Purāṇa, Aṃśa 2, Chapter 1).

<TEXT> devy{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>

        <PARAL>ŁTestimonia for this chapter:    \msCa\ ff.\thinspace 208v--210r,

        <!-- <TR>similarly to Indra's murder of the Brahmin [Viśvarūpa],

<APP><LEM>°phalā smṛtā</LEM> \msCc; °phalaḥ smṛtaḥ \msCapcorr\msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc,                                                °phala smṛtaḥ \msCaacorr, °pradaḥ smṛtaḥ \Ed</APP>
                 <PARAL>\vcd ŁSee e.g.\ \BhP\ 6.9.6: $ brahmahatyām{ }añjalinā jagrāha yad{ }apīśvaraḥ|
                                    saṃvatsarānte tad{ }aghaṃ bhūtānāṃ sa viśuddhaye|
                                    bhūmyambudrumayoṣidbhyaś{ }caturdhā vyabhajad{ }dhariḥ||</PARAL>
                 <NOTE>Context: Viśvarūpa was a son of Tvaṣṭṛ. Viśvarūpa's heads were struck off by Indra. 
                         In the Bhāgavatapurāṇa, Indra's sin are distributed among the ground, 
                         water, trees and women.</NOTE>
         % BhP 6.9.5:  ``Thereafter, the head meant for drinking soma-rasa was transformed into a kapiñjala [francolin partridge]. Similarly, the head meant for drinking wine was transformed into a kalaviṅka [sparrow], and the head meant for eating food became a tittiri [common partridge].''

<TEXT> sādhanaṃ śivasaṃkalpo yogasiddhiphalapradaḥ|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>The Śivasaṃkalpa [hymn] is practice (sādhana), 
                     which yields fruits of yoga accomplishments.</TR> -->
        <APP>\vd <LEM>°daḥ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb\msNc; °dam \Ed</APP>
        <NOTE>The Śivasaṃkalpa is Ṛgvedakhila 4.11 ff:
        yenedam bhūtaṃ bhuvanaṃ bhaviṣyat parigṛhītam amṛtena sarvam,
        yena yajñas tāyate saptahotā tan me manaś śivasaṅkalpam astu, etc. 
        See also Manu 11.251ab: sakṛt japtvāsyavāmīyaṃ śivasaṃkalpam eva ca.</NOTE>
% Monier-Williams: śivasaṃkalpa (śiva-) m. ‘auspicious in meaning’, N. of the text, VS. xxxii, 1-6 (also °pasūkta; also °popaniṣad; cf. Mn. xi, 251).
% perhaps they do practise the recitation of the Śivasaṃkalpa? Yes, see VSS 6.5 above?
        %Kristen: This is the relevant section of Scheftelowitz (Die Apokryphen des R̥gveda, 1906): https://archive.org/details/in.ernet.dli.2015.134238/page/n125/mode/1up. Unfortunately, the digitization leaves much to be desired (in other words, it's kind of illegible).  The hymn with Sāyaṇa's commentary is in vol. 4 of the Pune R̥g-Veda (https://ia800800.us.archive.org/25/items/RgVedaWithSayanasCommentaryPart4/rv_sayanabhasya_part4.pdf). There's also a translation in Usha Bhise's The Khila-Sūktas of the R̥g-Veda (BORI, 1995), but it is sitting uselessly on my external hard drive in Leiden.
        % Kenji: I found a short description of Śivasasṃkalpa in Tsuji’s Existent Yajurveda-Literature. 1970.
        p. 70.
        Śivasaṃkalpa (Vājasaneyīsaṃhitā XXXIV.1-6)
        ・This hymn regards Manas as the highest deity.
        ・Refrain of tan me manaḥ śivasaṃkalpam astu 
        ・Judging from the fact that it is not admitted by Vājasaneyīsaṃhitā of the Kāṇvas, it might be of later origin.
        ・Later expanded to 13 verses (die kāśmirische Rezension) or 28 verses. 
        ・Regarded as the Khila of the RV.
        ・verses 7–13: imitation using the refrain, verses 14–28 Śiva (=Manas) as the highest deity.
        cf. also p. 179 fn. 656-658.
        % CsK: Scheftelowitz, Isidor: »Śivasaṅkalpopaniṣad.« In: Zeitschrift der Deutschen Morgenländischen Gesellschaft 75 (1921), pp. 201-212. DOWNLOADED
        %NiśvGuhya: pāvamānīṃ ca japtavyā śivasaṃkalpa paścime 2:77
%% According to Brunner (1998:126, fn.312), pāvamānī is the
%% 9th maṇḍala of the ṚgVeda. (Can this be right?)
%% Note that 77 gives what the Ṛgvedin recites, 78 the Yajurvedin,
%% 79 the Sāmavedin, and 80 the Ātharvana.
        % CsK: the Śivasaṃkalpa is mentioned in a number of texts: Purāṇas, NiśvGuhy, Pauṣkara, Kālottara etc.

<TEXT> atha kenāpi kālena sūryarāgam{ }abhūt{ }tataḥ|</TEXT> 
        <!-- <TR>Now, once there was an eclipse of the sun.</TR> -->
% uparāga is eclipse
% kṛṣṇe?
<TEXT> grastabhāgatrayas{ }tv{ }āsīt{ }kṛṣṇamādhavamāsike||</TEXT> 12.8

<TEXT> iti śrutvā vacas{ }tasya vipulo vipulekṣaṇaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> vepamāno bhayatrasta aśrupūrṇākulekṣaṇaḥ||</TEXT>
        <APP>\vc <LEM>bhayatrasta</LEM> \Ed; bhayas{ }tatra \msCa</APP>
<TEXT> praṇamya śirasā bhūmau praṇipatya punaḥ punaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> uvāca madhuraṃ vākyaṃ brahmaloke pitāmaham||</TEXT>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>°loke</LEM> \Ed; °loka \msCa</APP>

<TEXT> vipula uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> bhagavan{ }sarvalokeśa sarvalokapitāmaha|</TEXT>

<TEXT> smṛtibhraṃśaś{ }ca me jāto buddhir{ }jātāndhacetanā|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>jātāndhacetanā</LEM> \msCa; jāto 'ndhacetanaḥ \Ed</APP>

        <APP>\vcd <LEM>(mūḍhoŁ...$ parāt{ }param)</LEM> \Ed; \om\ \msCa</APP>

        <APP>\vc <LEM>rogā°</LEM> \msCa; °rāgā° \Ed</APP>

        <APP>\vb <LEM>viśvebhir</LEM> \Ed; viśveśvi \msCa</APP>

<CHAPTER>13 garbhotpattiḥ</CHAPTER> 
<TEXT> devy{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> ahiṃsātithyakānāṃ ca śruto dharmaḥ suvistaraḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kiṃ na kurvanti manujāḥ sukhopāyaṃ mahat{ }phalam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> svaśarīrasthito yajñaḥ svaśarīre sthitaṃ tapaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> svaśarīre sthitaṃ tīrthaṃ śruto vistarato mayā||</TEXT>
<TEXT> kimarthaṃ bhagavan{ }brūhi sukhopāyaṃ mahat{ }phalam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kiṃ nivṛttās{ }tu deveśa ṛṣidaivatamānuṣāḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> mahādeva uvāca|*</TEXT>
        <APP>\vo <LEM>mahādeva</LEM> \msCa; bhagavān \Ed</APP>
<TEXT> adya pṛṣṭena kathitaṃ gopitaṃ ṛṣi sundari|</TEXT>
<TEXT> mānuṣāṇāṃ hitārthāya tava ca varavarṇini||</TEXT>
<TEXT> adyaprabhṛti deveśi khyātir{ }loke bhaviṣyati|</TEXT>
<TEXT> dhanyā evaṃ cariṣyanti adhanyā na ramanti tam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> triguṇena tu bandhena baddhā pāśadṛḍhena tu|</TEXT>
<TEXT> tenārthena ramanty{ }atra jānanto 'pi vimohitāḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> devy{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
% cchedaka would be unmetrical?
<TEXT> kiṃ vā triguṇabandheti brūhi saṃśayachedaka|</TEXT>
<TEXT> adyāpi mama deveśa mohotpannas{ }tribandhanaiḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> bhagavān{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> prākṛtaṃ vaikṛtaṃ caiva dakṣiṇābandham{ }eva ca|</TEXT>
<TEXT> etenaiva tu bandhena baddhāḥ varṇāśramāḥ sadā||</TEXT>
<TEXT> jñānahīnā nivartante paramaṃ prāpya tatparam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> iṣṭastrīṇā nivartante dhanadhānyasamuccaye|</TEXT>
<TEXT> snehād{ }ākṛṣya manasāṃ bandhaḥ prākṛta ucyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> yogayuktena manasā yad{ }yad{ }aiśvaryam{ }āpyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> tac{ }ca vaikṛtabandhas{ }tu yadi tatrānurajyate||</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.630
<TEXT> ārāmodyānavāpīṣu dānakratuphaleṣu ca|</TEXT>
%                        should be bandha metri causa
<TEXT> āśaktamanasā vācā dakṣiṇābandhaḥ kathyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> anenaiva tu pāśena baddhāvānaravad{ }yathā|</TEXT>
<TEXT> mokṣitaṃ na ca śaknoti itaś{ }cetaś{ }ca dhāvati||</TEXT>
<TEXT> devāsuramanuṣyeṣu tiryeṣu narakeṣu ca|</TEXT>
<TEXT> bhramante cakrayantreva ? yāvat{ }tattvaṃ na vindati||</TEXT>
<TEXT> garbhavāsaparikleśau janmamṛtyu punaḥ punaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> vyādhiḥ śokabhayāyāsa cintayā jarayā hataḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> devy{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> garbhotpattiḥ kathaṃ deva yogī labhati kīdṛśīm|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kīdṛśaṃ labhate garbhaḥ śrotuṃ naḥ pratyudīryatām||</TEXT>
<TEXT> bhagavān{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> śṛṇu devi pravakṣyāmi garbhotpattir{ }yathākramam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> yathā saṃśayavicchedaṃ bhaviṣyasi varānane||</TEXT>
<TEXT> akṣarāt{ }prabhavo brahmā karmabaddhasamudbhavam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> karmato yajñaprabhavo yajñato dhūmasambhavaḥ||</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>From ritual arises sacrifice. From sacrifice arises smoke.</TR> -->
<TEXT> parjanyād{ }annam{ }utpattir{ }annād{ }bhūtāni jajñire|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>From the clouds food arises. From food living beings arise.</TR> -->
<TEXT> annād{ }rasasamutpatti rasāc{ }choṇitasambhavaḥ||</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>From food arises rasa. From rasa arises blood.</TR> -->
<TEXT> śoṇitāt - māṃsa-m-utpatti māṃsād{ }medasamudbhavaḥ|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>From blood flesh arises. From flesh fat arises.</TR> -->
<TEXT> medaso 'sthīni jāyante asthibhyo majjasambhavaḥ||</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>From fat bones arise. From the bones marrow arises.</TR> -->
<TEXT> majjāyās{ }tu bhavec{ }chukraṃ naraḥ śukrasamudbhavaḥ|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>From marrow arises semen. And man is born from semen.</TR> -->
<TEXT> śukraśoṇitasaṃyogād{ }garbhotpattis{ }tataḥ smṛtaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> agnisomātmakaṃ devi śarīradvayadhātutaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> somadhātusmṛtaṃ śukram{ }agnidhāturajasmṛtam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> agnisomāśrayaṃ devi śarīram{ }iti saṃjñitam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> māsī māsī ṛtuḥ strīṇāṃ bhavatīha na saṃśayaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> ṛtukāle prasarpyeta na sukhārthaṃ varānane||</TEXT>
<TEXT> putrakāmaprayuñjīta dharmārthaś{ }ca yaśasvini|</TEXT>
<TEXT> pumān{ }strīpuṃ prayuñjīta araṇī bahutāśanaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> pumān{ }śukrādhiko jñeyaḥ kanyā raktādhikā bhavet|</TEXT>
<TEXT> samaśukre ca rakte ca sa ca jāyen{ }napuṃsakaḥ||</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.631

<SUBCHAPTER>dviyamā triyamā ca gurviṇī</SUBCHAPTER>
<TEXT> devy{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> dviyamā triyamā caiva kathaṃ jāyeta gurviṇī|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kathaṃ strīdviyamā jāyet{ }kathaṃ vā puruṣadvayam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> bhagavān{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> raktādhikā smṛtā kanyā jāyate varavarṇini|</TEXT>
<TEXT> vāyunā ca dvidhā bhinnā kanyakadviyamā smṛtā||</TEXT>
<TEXT> śukrādhikās{ }tu puruṣa dvidhā bhinnānilena tu|</TEXT>
<TEXT> dviyamā puruṣo jñeyā triyamās{ }tu tridhā kṛte||</TEXT>
<TEXT> ṛtusnātā yadā nārī yadi garbhādi gṛhyati|</TEXT>
<TEXT> prathame ca dvitīye ca tṛtīye ca sa jīvati||</TEXT>
<TEXT> sameṣu janayet{ }putraḥ kanyakā viṣame dine|</TEXT>
<TEXT> ṣaṣṭyāṣṭamau ca daśamī dvādaśī ca pumān{ }bhavet||</TEXT>
<TEXT> pañcamī saptamī caiva navamekādaśī striyaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> samarakte ca śukre ca śyāmaḥ saṃjāyate pumān||</TEXT>
<TEXT> rudhiraṃ tv{ }ekarātreṇa kalalaṃ pratipadyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kalalaṃ pañcarātreṇa arbudatvaṃ prajāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> arbudaḥ saptarātreṇa māṃsapeśī samudbhavaḥ|</TEXT>
% \kb\ Śivadharmottara 29ab
<TEXT> dvitīyaṃ saptarātreṇa tat{ }sarvaṃ māṃsaśoṇitam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> tṛtīyaṃ saptarātreṇa hṛdayaṃ jāyate tataḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> tataḥ sarvāṇi gātrāṇi śiraś{ }caivopajāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> hṛdaye jāyamāne tu mūrcchāntandrirarocakaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> striyāḥ dhardiḥ praśekaś{ }ca daurbalyaṃ copajāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> tasyā hi hṛdayaṃ nārī yadi bhakṣyati kiṃcana|</TEXT>
% MSS bhidyati 
% PREZI CHECK
<TEXT> bhakṣyaṃ lohyaṃ tathā peyam{ }upabhogās{ }tathāyayat||</TEXT>
% lehyaṃ
<TEXT> śayanāsanayānāni vastrāṇy{ }ābharaṇāni ca|</TEXT>
<TEXT> yad{ }yad{ }ākāṃkṣate kiṃcit{ }tat{ }tad{ }āsyai pradāpayet||</TEXT>
        <PARAL> \vo ŁCf.\ MBh 13.40.12:$
        śayyāsanam alaṃkāram annapānam anāryatām
        durvāgbhāvaṃ ratiṃ caiva dadau stgrībhyaḥ prajāpatiḥ</PARAL>
% read pānāni? see Bṛhatkālottara Gaurīyāna 90

<TEXT> nāyā saṃkārayec{ }cāsyā na caivam{ }avamānayet|</TEXT>
<TEXT> mukham{ }āpāṇḍuraṃ snigdhaṃ kapolastanakeśayoḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> śarīraś{ }ca śriyā jaṣṭuṃ pīnoruśroṇi vakṣasam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> liṅgerebhir{ }vijānīyāṃ garbhe jīvaṃ pratiṣṭhitam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> caturthe saptarātreṇa śiraś{ }caivopajāyate|</TEXT>
% unmetr (two short)
<TEXT> pañcamasaptarātreṇa grīvā tatropajāyate||</TEXT>
% unmetr (two short)
<TEXT> ṣaṣṭhamasaptarātreṇa skandhagātraṃ prajāyate|</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.632
<TEXT> saptamasaptarātreṇa pṛṣṭhavaṃśa prajāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> aṣṭamasaptarātreṇa pāṇī jāyate cobhayau|</TEXT>
<TEXT> saptarātraṃ nava prāpya jāyate hṛdi pañjaram||</TEXT>
<TEXT> daśame saptarātre ca pādau jāyate cobhau|</TEXT>
<TEXT> udaraś{ }copajāyeta saptaikādaśarātrike||</TEXT>
% unmetr (two short)
<TEXT> dvādaśasaptarātreṇa kukṣipārśveḥ prajāyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> saptatraidaśarātreṇa kuṭisutropajāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> navaty{ }aṣṭamarāteṇa jāyate sūtraviṃśati|</TEXT>
<TEXT> saptapañcadaśāhena sarvamedaḥ prajāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> ṣoḍaśasaptarātreṇa athisarvāṇi jāyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> saptasaptadaśāhena jāyate snāyubandhanam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> saptamāṣṭādaśāhena jāyate mukhamaṇḍalam|</TEXT>

<TEXT> saptaviṃśatirātreṇa naitranāliṃ prajāyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> saptaikaviṃśarātreṇa karṇayugmaṃ prajāyate||</TEXT>

<TEXT> unaviṃśatisaptāhe jāyate ca tvag{ }eva ca||</TEXT>
% unmetr (two short)
<TEXT> triṃśatasaptarātreṇa jāyate nābhimaṇḍalam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> saptaikatriṃśarātreṇa sarvarandhraṃ prajāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> dvātriṃśasaptarātreṇa nakhaviṃśati jāyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> tritriṃśasaptarātreṇa sarve sandhiḥ prajāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> pañcatriṃśati saptāhe sarvamarma prajāyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> ṣaḍtriṃśasaptarātreṇa vedanā copajāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> saptatriṃśatisaptāhe īrṣyādveṣaḥ prajāyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> aṣṭatriṃśatisaptāhe pañcātmakasamanvitam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> sarvāṅgam{ }aṅgasampūrṇaḥ paripakva(ḥ) sa tiṣṭhati|</TEXT>
<TEXT> mātusvāśitapītaś{ }ca nābhisūtrāganena tu||</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.633
<TEXT> ajātasyopadhāryante garbhasthasyaiva jantavaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> tataḥ praviśate dehe nidrāsvapna yathā tathā||</TEXT>

<TEXT> nopalabhyati sūkṣmatvād{ }araṇy{ }agnir{ }yathā tathā|</TEXT>
<TEXT> garbhodakena siktāṅgajarāyā pariveṣṭitaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> jāti smarati tatrastho jantuś{ }cetaḥsamanvitaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> mṛtaś{ }cāhaṃ punarjāto bhūyaś{ }caiva punarmṛtaḥ||</TEXT>
% \kb\ Śivadharmottara 39ab 
<TEXT> sthāvarāṇāṃ sahasreṣu jāto 'smi vividheṣu ca|</TEXT>
<TEXT> caturvarṇavivarṇeṣu mānuṣeṣu sahasraśaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> sāmprataṃ ca punar{ }garbhaḥ kleśaḥ prāptaḥ suduḥsahaḥ|</TEXT>

% similar to Śivadharmottara 40ab
<TEXT> yogam{ }evābhisevāmi sā[ṃ]khyaṃ vā pañcaviṃśakam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> yatra janmajarā nāsti yatra mṛtyuś{ }ca nāsti vai||</TEXT>
<TEXT> yatra brahma paraṃ vedyaṃ cariṣyāmi yatavrataḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> evam{ }ādīny{ }anekāni cintayitvā punaḥ punaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> yāvat{ }tiṣṭhati garbhastho jāti smarati pūrvikām|</TEXT>
<TEXT> tato jāyati kaṣṭena mahākleśena mānavaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> yoniyantrasutīvreṇa pīḍyamānasuduḥkhitaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> jātamātrosmṛtibhraṃśo bhavatīha acetaneḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> māyāmudgaratīvreṇa hataḥ kiṃ śubham{ }ācaret|</TEXT>
<TEXT> eṣa garbhasamutpattiḥ kathito 'smi varānane|</TEXT>
<TEXT> duḥkhasaṃsārapraśamaṃ kiṃ bhūyaḥ śrotum{ }icchasi||</TEXT>

%chapter 14
%Naraharinatha p.633
<ANUSTUBH/>
<CHAPTER>14 praśnavyākaraṇam</CHAPTER> 
<TEXT> devy{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
% unmetr licence hr
<TEXT> atidīrghātihrasvaś{ }ca pumān{ }kenopajāyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> atigauro 'tikṛṣṇaś{ }ca naro bhavati kiṃ prabho||</TEXT>
<TEXT> bhagavān{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> gṛhītagarbhā yā nārī nityam{ }uttānaśālinī|</TEXT>
<TEXT> prasāritavimuktātmā so 'tidīrghaḥ prajāyate||</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.634
<TEXT> gṛhītagarbhā yā nārī śete saṃkucitā sadā|</TEXT>
<TEXT> raso 'nnādīni kaṭukaṃ sevanāḥ hrasva jāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> gṛhītagarbhā yā nārī nityaṃ kṣīropasevitā|</TEXT>
<TEXT> varakodravaśālī ca bhuktā cāpi yavodanam||</TEXT>
% sāti- ! for sa ati double sandhi
<TEXT> śuklavastrasrajā yuktā sātigauraṃ prajāyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> gṛhītagarbhā yā nārī bāladhānyāni sevate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> kṛṣṇakodravatailādi māṣakṛṣṇayavodanam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kṛṣṇavastrasrajādīni tasyāḥ kṛṣṇaḥ prajāyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> devy{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> jātyandho jāyate kasmānṣaṇḍhobhīrur{ }hatendriyaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kujo vā vāmano vāpi paṅgavaḥ sthūlaśiraḥ katham||</TEXT>
<TEXT> bhagavān{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> gṛhītagarbhā yā nārī tīkṣṇoṣṇāny{ }upasevate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> laśunānipalāṇḍūni karañjamūlakāni ca||</TEXT>

<TEXT> puṃsā kapolaromāni khalitaṃ kena jāyate|</TEXT>

<TEXT> chāyāvyapagatasnehā rukṣāgātraśiroruhā|</TEXT>
<TEXT> grasatosmābhajaṭharā mṛtagarbhaḥ prajāyate||</TEXT>

<TEXT> somadhātu kathaṃ jñeyā agnidhātus{ }tatheśvara|</TEXT>

<TEXT> śleṣmamedas{ }tathā snāyuḥ asthidantanakhāni ca|</TEXT>

<TEXT> eteṣāṃ saumyabhāgatvāc{ }chvetatvam{ }upajāyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> āgneyabhāvād{ }raktatvaṃ kṛṣṇatvaṃ cāpi gacchati||</TEXT>

<TEXT> āgneyadhātusomaś{ }ca kathito 'smi varānane|</TEXT>

                 It is supportless, it is not contained in anything, it is unparalleled and spotless.</TR> -->

<TEXT> tadvaj{ }jīvo na paśyeta śarīrastho 'pi sundari||</TEXT> 15.5
        <APP>\vc <LEM>jīvo na</LEM> \msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc; jīvon{ }na \msCa, jīvaṃ na \Ed</APP>

        <!-- <TR>As fire [hidden] in fire-kindling sticks[?] is not perceivable in the wood,

        <NOTE>Note Łpaśyeta$ as a passive form.</NOTE>

<TEXT> dadhivac{ }ca yathā sarpir{ }dṛśyate na ca dṛśyate|</TEXT>

        <!-- <TR>Just as ghee can and cannot be seen in[?] curd[?],
                 in the same way the soul in the body can and cannot be seen.</TR> -->

        <APP>\vc <LEM>dṛśyate°</LEM> \msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc; dṛśyete° \msCa, dṛśyante \Ed</APP>

        <!-- <TR>It is doubtlessly pervasive, omnipresent, it is Śiva.
                  It can be perceived through its contact with the senses. [That is] the direct perception of the evidence of
                        [the existence of] the soul.</TR> -->

<TEXT> yathākāśasthito vāyuḥ śabdasparśaguṇānvitaḥ|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vcd <LEM>vāyuḥ śabda°</LEM> \msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; vāyu<UNCL>śśa</UNCL>¤ \msCa</APP>

<TEXT> tadvad{ }dehī vijānīyād{ }guṇaceṣṭena nānyathā||</TEXT> 15.9
        <APP>\vd <LEM>°ceṣṭena</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb; °veṣṭana \msNc, °veṣṭena \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>As air in the sky is endowed with the qualities of sound and touch,
                 similarly one can perceive the soul through the functioning of its qualities and in no other way.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Although it is difficult to be certain whether the majority of the MSS read °Łceṣṭena$ or Ł°veṣṭena$,
                        I suppose that the somewhat irregular Ł°ceṣṭena$ is the right reading 
                        and that it stands for a more standard Ł°ceṣṭayā$.</NOTE>

                 [I suppose] you said that [only] idly. In this case, why does [the soul] die?</TR> -->

% \msNa\ reads bhagavān too!

<TEXT> na jīvo mriyate devi sarveṣāṃ surasundari|</TEXT>
% na jīvo mriyate' (Chāndogya 6.11.3) CHECK

<TEXT> ghaṭāntastho yathākāśo bahirākāśavad{ }yathā||</TEXT> 15.11
        <!-- <TR>O Goddess, nobody's soul ever dies, O Surasundarī.
                 As [in the case of] space inside a pot, and space outside it,</TR> -->


 %% Caryāmelāpakapradīpa of Āryadeva:
        yathā dīpo ghaṭāntaḥstho bāhye naivāvabhāsate /
        bhinne tu tadghaṭe paścād dīpajvālābhibhāsate //
        svakāya eva hi ghaṭo dīpa eva hi tattvakam /
        guruvaktreṇa saṃbhinne buddhajñānaṃ sphuṭaṃ bhavet //
        gaganaṃ gaganodbhūtam ākāśākāśaṃ sa paśyati /
        tathaiva hi guror vaktrāt prayogo 'yaṃ pradarśitaḥ //

<TEXT> ghaṭabhinne viśālākṣi viśeṣo nopalakṣyate|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>nopalakṣyate</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNb\msNc\Ed; nopalabhyate \msNa</APP>

<TEXT> dehabhinne yadā devi vināśo nopalabhyate||</TEXT> 15.12
<APP>\vc <LEM>deha°</LEM> \msCa\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; dehe \msCb</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>yadā devi</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc; tathā dehī \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>there is no perceivable difference when the pot is broken to pieces, O Viśālākṣī.
                  [Similarly,] when the body perishes, O goddess, there is no perceivable destruction [of the soul].</TR> -->
        <PARAL>\vo Łcf.\ Bhāgavatapurāṇa 12.5.5: $
                         ghaṭe bhinne ghaṭākāśa ākāśaḥ syād yathā purā|
                         evaṃ dehe mṛte jīvo brahma sampadyate punaḥ||</PARAL>

<TEXT> susūkṣmaḥ sarvago vyāpī paramātmānam{ }avyayaḥ|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>susūkṣmaḥ</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb; susūkṣma \msNc, sa sūkṣmaḥ \Ed</APP>
\msCbacorr paramānmāna vyaya

<TEXT> bahir{ }antaś{ }ca bhūtānām{ }acaraś{ }cara eva saḥ||</TEXT> 15.13
<APP>\vd <LEM>°caraś{ }ca°</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc; °caran{ }ca° \Ed</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>saḥ</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc; sa \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>It is extremely subtle, omnipresent, pervasive, it is the supreme soul, it is imperishable.
             It is outside and inside the living beings. It is immovable and moving.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Note Łparamātmānam$ for Łparamātmā$.</NOTE>

<TEXT> aprameyo 'vināśī ca aprapañcaḥ prapañcakaḥ|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vab <LEM>(aprameyoŁ...$ prapañcakaḥ)</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNc\Ed; \om\ \msNb</APP>

<TEXT> sarvendriyaguṇābhāsaḥ sarvendriyavivarjitaḥ||</TEXT> 15.14
        <!-- <TR>It is immeasurable, imperishable, unmanifest and manifest.
                 It appears as having the qualities of all the senses but is devoid of senses.</TR> -->

<TEXT> evam{ }eṣa mahādevi jīvasya varavarṇini|</TEXT>

<TEXT> kathito 'smi samāsena kim{ }anyac{ }chrotum{ }icchasi||</TEXT> 15.15
        <APP>\vd <LEM>icchasi</LEM> \msCb\msNa\msNb\msNc\Ed; icchati \msCa</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Thus have I briefly described to you, O Mahādevī, the soul. O Varavarṇinī,
                what else would you like to hear?</TR> -->


<SUBCHAPTER>sāraśreṣṭham</SUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBCHAPTER>The best</TRSUBCHAPTER>

        <!-- <TR>O Mahādeva, O Īśāna, Īśvara! Tell me what is the best in essence.
                I would like to hear it, O Deveśa. Tell me for the benefit of mankind.</TR> -->

                        the non-standard form Łanāśanas$.</NOTE>

<TEXT> devy{ }uvāca|*</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>The goddess spoke:</TR> -->

<TEXT> adhunā śrotum{ }icchāmi yogasadbhāvanirṇayam|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>Now I would like to hear the exposition of the essence of yoga.</TR> -->
        <PARAL>\vo Ł  \msCa\ 435.jpg line 2; \msCb\ 448.jpg line 2;
                      This chapter is missing in \msCc.
                      \msNa\ 220.jpg lower image line 5; \msNb\ 65.jpg upper image line 6.$</PARAL>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°nirṇayam</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb; °nirṇayaḥ \Ed</APP>

% the things you actually do, theory, Francesco;  check Niśvā: preparation of the body Nirajan 
<TEXT> karaṇaṃ ca yathānyāyaṃ kathayasva sureśvara||</TEXT> 16.1
        <!-- <TR>Furthermore teach me about the Karaṇa [exercises, practice?], according to the rules, O Sureśvara.</TR> -->
        % What is karaṇa? Simply āsana?
        <APP>\vc <LEM>karaṇaṃ</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb; karaṇaś \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>sureśvara</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb; sureśvaraḥ \Ed</APP>
        % see Kafle thesis p36 on karaṇa

<TEXT> prayāti lokaṃ jagadīśvarasya</TEXT>

<TEXT> annaprado modati devaloke||</TEXT>

<TEXT> cyutaś{ }ca martye sa bhaved{ }dhanāḍhyaḥ</TEXT>
<TEXT> kulodgataḥ sarvaguṇopapannaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> yaśaḥ śriyaṃ sarvakalajñatā ca</TEXT>
<TEXT> bhavet{ }sa bhogī sakalatraputraḥ||</TEXT>

<TEXT> dadyād{ }daridraḥ kṛpaṇārtadīno</TEXT>
<TEXT> bālāgadatvāturamāgatānām|</TEXT>
<TEXT> tṛṣṇābubhukṣāgatikāgatānām</TEXT>
<TEXT> dattvā sadharmasya phalaṃ kaniṣṭa||</TEXT>

<TEXT> vāṇijyadharmādiphalāśritānām</TEXT>
<TEXT> dharmo hi tasya na ca nirmalo 'sti|</TEXT>
<TEXT> toyaṃ ca dadyāl{ }laghupūrṇakambham</TEXT>
<TEXT> śītaṃ sugandhaṃ parivāritaṃ ca||</TEXT>

<TEXT> sa yāti lokaṃ salileśvarasya</TEXT>
<TEXT> na tasya janmānitṛṣābhibhūtaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> upānahaṃ yo dadati dvijāya</TEXT>

<TEXT> suśobhanaṃ tailasudī surapitaṃ ca||</TEXT>

<TEXT> te yānti lokam{ }amarādhipasya</TEXT>
<TEXT> yamālayaṃ kaṣṭapathāna yānti|</TEXT>
<TEXT> prakṣīṇapuṇyā punar{ }atra loke</TEXT>
<TEXT> jāto bhaved{ }divyakulopapannaḥ||</TEXT>

<TEXT> dhanaiḥ samṛddhodhopatitvatāś{ }ca</TEXT>
<TEXT> rathāś{ }ca nāgā prabhavanti tasya|</TEXT>
<TEXT> vastrapradānena bhavanti devi</TEXT>
<TEXT> rūpottamasarvakalajñatāṃ ca||</TEXT>

<TEXT> samṛddhisaubhāgyaguṇānvitāś{ }ca</TEXT>
<TEXT> svargacyutās{ }te puruṣā bhavanti|</TEXT>

<TEXT> śatajanmasahasrāṇi bhoktā bhavati madhyamaḥ||</TEXT>

<TEXT> uttamaḥ palabhoktā (phala?) vi ? janmakoṭiśatatrayam| </TEXT>
<TEXT> parārdhadvayajanmānāṃ bhoktā vai cottamottamaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> bhūtānām{ }anukampayā yadi dhanaṃ dātā sadānvarṣine|</TEXT>
<TEXT> dīnānvakṛyaṇeṣv{ }anāthamalineśvānādini?? ca||</TEXT>
% \msCa line 4

% śārdūla?
%       -     - -? . . -  . -  . . . -    -   -  . -    -  . -
<TEXT> yady{ }eva kurute sadārtiharaṇaṃ śraddhānvitau bhaktimān|</TEXT>
%       -  - -  . . -   . -  .  . .  -    -? -  .  -  -  . -
<TEXT> tasyānantayālaṃ vadanti vibudhāṃs sa yasya sandarśanāt||</TEXT>
<ANUSTUBH/>
<TEXT> <COLOPHON>iti vṛṣasārasaṃgrahe dānadharmaviśeṣaṃ nāma saptādaśamo 'dhyāyaḥ</COLOPHON></TEXT>

<CHAPTER>19 dānayajñaviśeṣaḥ</CHAPTER>
<TEXT> vigatarāga uvāca|*</TEXT>
% licence pra
<TEXT> kriyāsūkṣmo mahādharmaḥ karmaṇā kena prāpyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> alpopāyaṃ narārthāya pṛcchāmi kathayasva me||</TEXT>
<TEXT> anarthayajña uvāca|*</TEXT>
% māhā was typo?

<TEXT> sukhena labhate svargaṃ karmaṇā yena tac{ }chṛṇu||</TEXT>
<TEXT> lokānaṃ mātaro gāvo gobhiḥ sarvaṃ jagad{ }dhṛtam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> gomayam{ }amṛtaṃ sarvaṃ jātaṃ sarvaśivecchayā||</TEXT>
<TEXT> sarvadevamayī gāvaḥ sarvadevamayo dvijaḥ|</TEXT>

<TEXT> paricaryā yathāśaktyā grāsavāsajalādibhiḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> tāḍayen{ }nātivegena vācayen{ }mṛdunācaret|</TEXT>
<TEXT> pālayan{ }tarpanād{ }yeṣu bhagnodvigneṣu yatnataḥ||</TEXT>
% unmetr (two short)
<TEXT> vyādhivanaparikleśa oṣadhopakramaś{ }caret|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kaṇḍūyanaṃ ca kartavyaṃ yathāsaukhyaṃ bhaved{ }gavām||</TEXT>
<TEXT> gavāṃ pradakṣiṇaṃ kṛtvā śraddhābhaktisamanvitaḥ|</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.652
<TEXT> sāgarāntā mahī sarvā n{ }pradakṣiṇīkṛtā bhavet||</TEXT>
<TEXT> pṛṣṭasaṃsparśanād{ }yañ{ }ca śraddhayā yadi mānavaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> ahorātrakṛtaṃ pāpaṃ naśyate nātrasaṃśayaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> lāṅgūlenoddhṛtaṃ toyaṃ mūrddhnā gṛhṇāti yo naraḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> yāvaj{ }jīva kṛtaṃ pāpaṃ naśyate nātra saṃśayaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> vidhivat{ }snāpayed{ }gāṃś{ }ca mantrayuktena vāriṇā|</TEXT>
<TEXT> tenāmbhasā svayaṃ snātvā sarvapāpakṣayo bhavet||</TEXT>
<TEXT> vyādhivighnam{ }alakṣmītvaṃ naśyate sadya eva ca|</TEXT>
<TEXT> mṛtāpatyāś{ }ca gāvāś{ }ca snānam{ }eva praśasyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> gavāṃ śṛṅgodakaṃ gṛhya mūrdhni yo dhārayen{ }naraḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> sa sarvatīrthasnānasya phalaṃ prāpnoti mānavaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> grāsamuṣṭipradānena goṣu bhaktisamanvitaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> agnihotraṃ hutaṃ tena sarvadevāḥ sutarpitāḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> catvāraḥ stanadhārās{ }tu yas{ }tu mūrdhnā pratīcchati|</TEXT>

<TEXT> śivalokaparibhraṣṭaḥ pṛthivyām{ }ekarāḍ{ }bhavet||</TEXT>

<TEXT> vigatarāga uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> devāḥ r aṣṭavidhāḥ proktāḥ tiryak{ }pañcavidhaḥ smṛtaḥ|</TEXT>

<TEXT> kartuṃ karma samārabdhakarmaś{ }cāpi vibhajyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> ṛtvajatve sthitāḥ kecit{ }kecit{ }saṃrakṣaṇe sthitāḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> arthopārjanayuktān{ }ye anye śilpe niyojitāḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> evaṃ yajñavidhānena kartum{ }arebhire purā|</TEXT>
<TEXT> yathoddiṣṭena karmeṇa yajñotsāham{ }avartata||</TEXT>
<TEXT> āgatā ṛṣayaḥ sarve devatāḥ pitaras{ }tathā|</TEXT>
<TEXT> anyonyam{ }abruvan{ }tatra devarṣipitṛdevatāḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> yajñārtam{ }asṛjad{ }varṇaṃ vidhinā pātuhetavaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> evam{ }eva pravartantu bhavatir{ }dvijasattamāḥ||</TEXT>
% hypermetr CHECK MSS
<TEXT> ijyādhyādhyayanasampannā brahmaṇā yatra kalpitāḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> suviprā vipratāṃ yāntu ṣaḍkarmāniratāḥ sadā||</TEXT>
<TEXT> rakṣaṇārtaṃ tu ye viprāḥ kalpitāḥ śastrapāṇayaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kṛtatrāṇāya viprāṇāṃ nityaṃ kṣātravratodbhavāḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> arthopārjanam{ }uddiśya kalpitā ye dvijātayaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> te tu vaiśyatvam{ }āyāntu vārto āpaṇatodbhavāḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> vadhabandhanakarmeṣu śilpasthānavadheṣu ca||</TEXT>
<TEXT> kalpitā ye dvijātīnāṃ sarve śūdrā bhavantu te|</TEXT>
<TEXT> prājāpatyaṃ brāhmaṇānām{ }ījyādhyayanatatparām||</TEXT>
<TEXT> sthānam{ }aindraṃ kṣatriyāṇāṃ prajāpālanatatparam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> vaiśyānāṃ vāsavasthānaṃ vāṇijyaṃ kṛṣijīvinām||</TEXT>
<TEXT> śūdrāṇāṃ marutaḥ sthānaṃ śuśrūṣāniratātmanām|</TEXT>
<TEXT> maharṣipitṛdevānāṃ matam{ }ājñāya niścitaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> eṣa saṃkalpito brahmā padmayoniḥ pitāmahaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> saṃkalpaprabhavāḥ sarve devadānavamānavāḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> paśupakṣimṛgāmukhyā yāvanti jagasambhavāḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> bhūtasaṃkalpakartā ya kalpam{ }āsīd{ }dvijottama|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kīrtitāni samāsena kim{ }anyac{ }chrotum{ }icchasi||</TEXT>
<TEXT> vigatarāga uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> kiṃ tapaḥ sarvavarṇānāṃ vṛttir{ }vāpi tapodhana|</TEXT>
<TEXT> yajñāś{ }caiva pṛthaktvena śrotum{ }icchāmi tattvataḥ||</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.654
<TEXT> anarthayajña uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> brāhmaṇasya tapo yajñāḥ - tapaḥ kṣātrasya rakṣaṇam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> vaiśyaś{ }ca tapa vāṇijya tapaḥ śūdrasya sevanam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> pratigraha dhano vipraḥ kṣatriyasya dhanur{ }dhanam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kṛṣir{ }dhanaṃ tathā vaiśyaḥ śūdraḥ śuśrūṣaṇaṃ dhanam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> ārambhayajñaḥ kṣatrasya havir{ }yajño viśas{ }tathā|</TEXT>
        <PARAL>\vab Ł \kb\ MBh 12224061ab and 12230012ab $ </PARAL>
<TEXT> śūdraḥ paricaro yajño japayajño dvijātayaḥ||</TEXT>
% a lot of nom. for gen, and stem forms
<TEXT> satya tīrtha dvijātīnāṃ raṇa tīrthaṃ tu kṣatriyāḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> āryā tīrthaṃ tu vaiśānāṃ ! śūdratīrthaṃ tu vai dvijāḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> nāsti vidyāsamo mitro nāsti dānasamaḥ sakhā|</TEXT>
<TEXT> nāsti jñānasamo bandur{ }nāsti yajño japaḥ samaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> dharmahīno mṛtas{ }tulyo devatulyo jitendriyaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> yajñatulyo 'bhayaṃ dātā śivatulyao manonmanaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> vigatarāga uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> dāna yajñas{ }tapas{ }tīrthaṃ saṃnyāsaṃ yoga eva ca|</TEXT>
<TEXT> eteṣu katamaḥ śreṣṭhaḥ śrotum{ }icchāmi kīrtaya||</TEXT>
<TEXT> anarthayajña uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> dānadharmasahasrebhyaḥ yajñayājī viśiṣyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> yajñayājīsahasrebhyas{ }tīrthayātrī viśiṣyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> tīrthayātrisahasrebhyas{ }tapaniṣṭo viśiṣyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> tapaniṣṭhasahasrebhyaḥ śreṣṭhaḥ saṃnyāsikaḥ smṛtaḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> saṃnyāsīnāṃ sahasrebhyaḥ śreṣṭho yac{ }ya jitendriyaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> jitendriyasahasrebhyaḥ yogayukto viśiṣyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> yogayuktasahasrebhyaḥ śreṣṭho līnamanaḥ smṛtaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> tasmāt{ }sarvaprayatnena ādau mana viśodhayet||</TEXT>
<TEXT> nigṛhītendriyagrāmaḥ svargamokṣau tu sādhanam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> viśiṣṭhe tv{ }indriyagrāme tiryannarakasādhanam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> vigatarāga uvāca|*</TEXT>
%hypometrical
<TEXT> carācarāṇāṃ bhūtānāṃ katamaḥ śreṣṭha ucyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kathayasva mamādya tvaṃ chettum{ }arhasi saṃśayam||</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.655
<TEXT> anarthayajña uvāca|*</TEXT>
<TEXT> carācarāṇāṃ bhūtānāṃ tatra śreṣṭho - carāḥ smṛtāḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> carāṇāṃ caiva sarveṣāṃ buddhimān{ }śreṣṭha ucyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> buddhimānṣu ! ca sarveṣu tataḥ śreṣṭha narāḥ smṛtāḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> narāṇāṃ caiva sarveṣāṃ brāhmaṇaḥ śreṣṭha ucyate||</TEXT>
% vidvatsu \msCc
<TEXT> vidvarsv{ }api ca sarveṣu kṛtabuddhir{ }viśiṣyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kṛtabuddhiṣu sarveṣu śreṣṭhaḥ kartā sa ucyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> kartṛṣv{ }api ca sarveṣu brahmavedī viśiṣyate|</TEXT>
<TEXT> brahmavedi paraṃ ! vipraḥ nānyaṃ vedmi paraṃtapaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> sa vipraḥ sa tapasvī ca sa yogī sa śivaḥ smṛtaḥ||</TEXT>

<TEXT> vigatarāga uvāca|*</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>Vigatarāga spoke:</TR> -->

% numbers singular!
<TEXT> pañcaviṃśati yat{ }tattvaṃ jñātum{ }icchāmi tattvataḥ|</TEXT>

<TEXT> kathayasva mamādya tvaṃ chidyate yena saṃśayaḥ||</TEXT> 20.1
        <!-- <TR>I would like to learn about the twenty-five Tattvas truely. 
                 Teach me now so that my doubts could be dispelled.</TR> -->
        <NOTE> This chapter echoes and is partly based on MBh 12.247.1-10 (Mokṣadharma, see
                        parallel passages in the apparatus):
                <sep/>
                        Łbhīṣma uvāca |<br/>
                        bhūtānāṃ guṇasaṃkhyānaṃ bhūyaḥ putra niśāmaya |<br/>
                        dvaipāyanamukhād bhraṣṭaṃ ślāghayā parayānagha ||$1<br/>
                        Łdīptānalanibhaḥ prāha bhagavān dhūmravarcase |<br/>
                        tato 'ham api vakṣyāmi bhūyaḥ putra nidarśanam ||$2<br/>
                        Łbhūmeḥ sthairyaṃ pṛthutvaṃ ca kāṭhinyaṃ prasavātmatā |<br/>
                        gandho gurutvaṃ śaktiś ca saṃghātaḥ sthāpanā dhṛtiḥ ||$3<br/>
                        Łapāṃ śaityaṃ rasaḥ kledo dravatvaṃ snehasaumyatā |<br/>
                        jihvā viṣyandinī caiva bhaumāpyāsravaṇaṃ tathā ||$4<br/>
                        Łagner durdharṣatā tejas tāpaḥ pākaḥ prakāśanam |<br/>
                        śaucaṃ rāgo laghus taikṣṇyaṃ daśamaṃ cordhvabhāgitā ||$5<br/>
                        Łvāyor aniyamaḥ sparśo vādasthānaṃ svatantratā |<br/>
                        balaṃ śaighryaṃ ca mohaś ca ceṣṭā karmakṛtā bhavaḥ ||$6<br/>
                        Łākāśasya guṇaḥ śabdo vyāpitvaṃ chidratāpi ca |<br/>
                        anāśrayam anālambam avyaktam avikāritā ||$7<br/>
                        Łapratīghātatā caiva bhūtatvaṃ vikṛtāni ca |<br/>
                        guṇāḥ pañcāśataṃ proktāḥ pañcabhūtātmabhāvitāḥ ||$8<br/>
                        Łcalopapattir vyaktiś ca visargaḥ kalpanā kṣamā |<br/>
                        sad asac cāśutā caiva manaso nava vai guṇāḥ ||$9<br/>
                        Łiṣṭāniṣṭavikalpaś ca vyavasāyaḥ samādhitā |<br/>
                        saṃśayaḥ pratipattiś ca buddhau pañceha ye guṇāḥ ||$10<br/>
        </NOTE>
