<SUBCHAPTER>puruṣaḥ-śivaḥ-brahmā (25)</SUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBCHAPTER>The Puruṣa/Śiva/Brahmā (25th)</TRSUBCHAPTER>

<TEXT> nādimadhyaṃ na cāntaṃ ca yan{ }na vedyaṃ surair{ }api|</TEXT>
<APP>\va <LEM>°madhyaṃ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\Ed; °madya \msNb</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>cāntaṃ ca</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb; cāntaś{ }ca \Ed</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>surair{ }api</LEM> \msCa\msCc\msNa\msNb\Ed; surer{ }api \msCb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>That which has no beginning, no middle part and no end, 
                and is not to be known even by the gods,</TR> -->

<TEXT> atisūkṣmo hy{ }atisthūlo nirālambo nirañjanaḥ||</TEXT> 20.3 
        <APP>\vc <LEM>hy{ }ati°</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\msNb\Ed; hy{ }adi° \msCc</APP>
        <!-- <TR>that which is extremely subtle and extremely large, supportless and spotless,</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Note that the key terms (Łādi, madhya, anta, sūkṣma$) in this verse are to be found in VSS 1.1ab:
                <sep/>
               Ł anādimadhyāntam anantapāraṃ<br/>
                 susūkṣmam avyaktajagatsusāram$</NOTE>

<TEXT> acintyaś{ }cāprameyaś{ }ca akṣarākṣaravarjitaḥ|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>inconceivable, immeasurable, imperishable, devoid of syllables,</TR> -->

<TEXT> sarvaḥ sarvagato vyāpī sarvam{ }āvṛtya tiṣṭhati||</TEXT> 20.4
        <APP>\vcd <LEM>(sarvaḥŁ...$ tiṣṭhati)</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb; \om\ \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>that which is everything and everywhere and that which is pervasive, 
                        exists covering everything.</TR> -->

<TEXT> sarvendriyaguṇābhāsaḥ sarvendriyavivarjitaḥ|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vab <LEM>sarve°Ł...$ varjitaḥ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb; \om\ \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>It appears to have the qualities of all the sense faculties
                         but is devoid of all sense faculties.</TR> -->

% -jaḥ is a bit suspicious; I take it as a-jaḥ
<TEXT> ajarāmarajaḥ śāntaḥ paramātmā śivo 'vyayaḥ||</TEXT> 20.5
        <APP>\vc <LEM>°jaḥ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\msNb; yaḥ \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>It is not subject to ageing, it is immortal and unborn. It is peaceful, it is 
                the supreme soul, it is undecaying Śiva.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>I take Łajarāmarajaḥ$ in Łpāda$ a as Łajaro 'maro 'ajaś ca$.</NOTE>

% go for brahma?
<TEXT> alakṣyalakṣaṇaḥ svastho brahmā puruṣasaṃjñitaḥ|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>brahmā</LEM> \msCa\msCb\Ed; brahma \msCc\msNa\msNb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>It is characterised by being unobservable, it is self-abiding, it is Brahmā,
                        it is called Puruṣa.</TR> -->

<TEXT> pañcaviṃśaḥ sa vijñeyo janmamṛtyuharaḥ prabhuḥ||</TEXT> 20.6
<APP>\vc <LEM>°viṃśaḥ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNb\Ed; °viṃśat \msNaacorr, °viṃśa \msNapcorr</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>sa vijñeyo</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNaacorr\msNb\Ed; sarvajñeyo \msNapcorr</APP>
        <!-- <TR>It is to be known as the twenty-fifth [Tattva], the Lord (Łprabhu$) who destroys death and rebirth.</TR> -->
% Viṣṇu is not mentioned

<TEXT> kalākalaṅkanirmukto vyomapañcāśavarjitaḥ|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>°nirmukto</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\Ed; °lirmukto \msNb</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°pañcāśa°</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNa\Ed; °pañcasa° \msNb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>He is free of the stain of having parts[?], and is devoid of the fifty voids.</TR> -->

%Naraharinatha p.656
<TEXT> jalapakṣī yathā toyair{ }na lipyeta jale caran|</TEXT>
<APP>\vcd <LEM>yathā toyair{ }na</LEM> \msCa\Ed; yathā toyī na \msCbacorr,                        yathā toyer{ }na \msCbpcorr, yathā toyai na \msCc\msNa, yadā toyai nna \msNb</APP>

        <APP>\vc <LEM>°ṣair{ }na</LEM> \msCa\msCb\msNa\Ed; °ṣai na \msCc, °ṣai nna \msNb</APP>

<SUBCHAPTER>ākāśaḥ (suṣiratvaṃ) śabdaś{ }ca (21-20)</SUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBCHAPTER>Space (hollowness) and Sound (21st--20th)</TRSUBCHAPTER>

        <NOTE>Note that from now on in this chapter, Łguṇa$ is used in the sense of the Łtanmātra$ of Sāṃkhya philosophy
        and that the word Łtanmātra$ does not occur in the VSS.</NOTE>

%%MMW  guṇa:
  an attribute of the 5 elements (each of which has its own peculiar quality or qualities as well as organ of sense
  thus 1. ether has śabda, or sound for its Guṇa and the ear for its organ
  2. the air has tangibility and sound for its Guṇas and the skin for its organ
  3. fire or light has shape or colour, tangibility, and sound for its Guṇas, and the eye for its organs
  4. water has flavour, shape, tangibility, and sound for its Guṇas, and the tongue for its organ
  5. earth has the preceding Guṇas, with the addition of its own peculiar Guṇa of smell, and the nose for its organ), Mn. i, 20 and 76-78
  MBh. xii, 6846 ff. [see 12.23.23?]
  Śakuntalā i, 1:
        yā sṛṣṭiḥ sraṣṭur ādyā vahati vidhi-hutaṃ yā havir yā ca hotrī
        ye dve kālaṃ vidhattaḥ śruti-viṣaya-guṇā yā sthitā vyāpya viśvam /
        yām āhuḥ sarva-bīja-prakṛtir iti yayā prāṇinaḥ prāṇavantaḥ
        pratyakṣābhiḥ prapannas tanubhir avatu vas tābhir aṣṭābhir īśaḥ // KSak_1.1 //p.2
  BhP. iii, 5, 35:
        BhP_03.05.035/1 jyotiṣāmbho 'nusaṃsṛṣṭaṃ vikurvad brahma-vīkṣitam
        BhP_03.05.035/2 mahīṃ gandha-guṇām ādhāt kāla-māyāṃśa-yogataḥ

Encyclopedia of Indian Philosophies. Vol. 4. Sāṃkhya. ed. Larson and Bhattacharya. p. 121-122:
``V.M. Bedekar has nicely summarized the differences between this sort of fluid Sāṃkhya and Yoga and later 
philosophical Sāṃkhya:
        "(i) In the *Mokṣadharma* Sāṃkhya, there is not always emphasized an absolute and clear-cut dualism as in the classical
        Sāṃkhya. Many of the teachers of the Sāṃkhya in the *Mokṣadharma* appear generrally to posit, at the apex, one single
        Principle or entity which overrides the dualism. (ii) The *Mokṣadharma* Sāṃkhya, often, speaks of the doctrine 
        of the eight Prakṛtis, as against the one Prakṛti of the classical Sāṃkhya. (iii) The doctrine of the *tanmātras*
        (subtle elements) does not seem to have yet developed. There is, however, a mention of the five objects of
        senses or the five qualities of the elements. (iv) The teaching regarding the number, place and functions of the
        phychical faculties like *manas*, *ahaṃkāra*, and *buddhi* does not appear to have been consolidated in the 
        *Mokṣadharma*. Different teachers have expressed different views on the subject. (v) The origin or the source of
        of the five senses of knowledge has not been fixed as in the classical Sāṃkhya."   ''
[See Bedekar. Introduction to the Śāntiparvan. p. ccxliii ]

Larson Classical Sāṃkhya p. 114 on guṇa:
Moreover, in the Moksadharma the term guna is used in
a variety of ways as Edgerton, Johnston and others have noticed.
It frequently appears, of course, in the standard use as "quality"
of the avyakta or prakrti — e.g., XII. 294,32; 293, 33-34.
The term appears also, however, in the sense of "quality" or
"aspect" of the gross elements — e.g., XII 244, 4; 267, 13-15.
Then, too, the term is used in the sense of vikära or
"secondary part" — e.g., XII. 295, 13-17; 267, 28-29. 106

p115
The next two terms — i.e., puru$a and
ätman — seem to be used interchangeably throughout the epic,
and they function both as cosmic and individual conceptions. 113

see also p188
ibid. p.72: "The classical doctrines of *prakṛti*, *satkāryovāda*, *tattvavikāra* and the *tanmātras* are 
not present in these early forms of Sāṃkhya."
ibid p73: (j) By the 7th or 8th century A.D., according to Frauwallner, Sāmkhya has seriously declined. After a gap of many
centuries, Sāmkhya has a kind of renaissance as evidenced in
the late Sāṃkhyapravacanasūtra and the work of Vijñānabhikṣu,
Mahādeva and Aniruddha.

p74. (d) Problem of the introduction of tanmātras.

MBh 12 (Śāntiparvan) Mokṣadharma = Chapters: 174- (168-?) - 365

Larson Classical Sāṃkhya p19: Garbe: by no means an older form, no preliminary stage of the "classical," that is, the real, pure Samkhya, but
an unclear, partly pointless mixed philosophy. 66 ; 44ff : Johnston's steps...: 4 (f) the great elements and the objects of the senses
are replaced in these later speculations by the tanmätras and the gross elements — probably because of influence from Vaiksikas.
p50 Frauwallner's stage 2 (no tanmātras yet)!

p188: In the older accounts of the tattvas the five gross elements functioned in place of the
tanmātras, and the remaining five tattvas were the objects of the
senses, which are left out of the classical Sāmkhya listing.

        <APP>\va <LEM>pāyu°</LEM> \msCa; pāpa° \Ed</APP>
<TEXT> saraktaphenilādīni pāyuśakti pramuñcate||</TEXT>
<APP>\vd <LEM>pāyuśakti</LEM> \Ed;  pāyucchakti \msCa</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>°muñcati</LEM> \msCa; °muñcate \Ed</APP>

<SUBSUBCHAPTER>upasthakarma (3)</SUBSUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>The action of the sexual organs (3rd)</TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>
<TEXT> upasthakarma ānandaṃ karoti jananaṃ prajā|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>ānandaṃ</LEM> \msCa; ānanda \Ed</APP>
% ānandaṅ
<TEXT> strīpuṃnapuṃsakaṃ caiva upasthaṃ kurute dvija||</TEXT>



<SUBSUBCHAPTER>vākkarma (2)</SUBSUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>The action of speaking (2nd)</TRSUBSUBCHAPTER>

<TEXT> vācā tu kurute karma navadhā dvijapuṅgava|</TEXT>
<TEXT> stutinindā praśaṃsā ca ākrośaḥ priya eva saḥ||</TEXT>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>ākrośaḥ</LEM> \Ed; ×krośaḥ \msCa</APP>
<TEXT> praśno 'nujñā tathākhyānam{ }āśīś{ }ca vidhayo nava|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>cā vidhayo nava</LEM> \eme; ca vidhayo naya \msCa, cāvidhiyo nayaḥ \Ed</APP>
<TEXT> etā navavidhā vāṇī kīrtito me dvijottama||</TEXT>




<SUBCHAPTER>manaś{ }conmanaś{ }ca (1)</SUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBCHAPTER>The mind and the non-mind (1st)</TRSUBCHAPTER>

<TEXT> adhunā kathayiṣyāmi manaso nava vai guṇān|</TEXT>

<TEXT> calopapattiḥ sthairaṃ ca visargakalpanākṣamā|</TEXT>
<APP>\vd <LEM>visarga°</LEM> \Ed; visarge \msCa</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>°kṣamā</LEM> \msCa; °samā \Ed</APP>

        <APP>\ve <LEM>cāśutā</LEM> \Ed; cāśutāñ \msCa</APP>
        <PARAL>\vcdef Ł = MBh 12.247.9 $ </PARAL> 

% sadasavvā? \msCa

        <APP>\va <LEM>iṣṭā°</LEM> \Ed; ×ṣṭā° \msCa</APP>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>samādhitā</LEM>  \msCa; samādhinā \Ed</APP>
        <PARAL>\vab Ł = MBh 12.247.10ab $</PARAL>

        <APP>\vd <LEM>conmana</LEM> \Ed; cotmana \msCa</APP>

<TEXT> manas{ }tv{ }indriyabhāvatve unmanastvam{ }atīndriye|</TEXT>

% variants!            ñ ca \msCa

<SUBCHAPTER>unmanaḥ</SUBCHAPTER>
<TRSUBCHAPTER>The elimination of the mind</TRSUBCHAPTER>

<TEXT> vigatarāga uvāca|*</TEXT>
% ma-vipulā
<TEXT> manaḥ svavedyaṃ lokānām{ }unmanas{ }tu na vidyate|</TEXT>

<TEXT> unmanaḥ kathayāsmākaṃ kīdṛśaṃ lakṣaṇaṃ bhavet||</TEXT>

<TEXT> anarthayajña uvāca|*</TEXT>

<TEXT> unmanastvaṃ gate vipra nibodha daśalakṣaṇam|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>nibodha</LEM> \Ed; ×bodha \msCa</APP>

<TEXT> na śabdaṃ śṛṇute śrotraṃ śaṅkhabherīsvanād{ }api||</TEXT>
        <APP>\vc <LEM>śrotraṃ</LEM> \msCa; śrotre \Ed</APP>
%Naraharinatha p.661

<TEXT> tvacaḥ sparśaṃ na jānāti śītoṣṇam{ }api duḥsaham|</TEXT>

<TEXT> rūpaṃ paśyati no cakṣuḥ parvatābhyadhiko 'pi vā||</TEXT>

<TEXT> jihvā rasaṃ na vindeta madhurāmlavato 'pi vā|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>°mlavato</LEM> \Ed; °mlavano \msCa</APP>

<TEXT> gandhaṃ jighrati na ghrāṇā tīkṣṇaṃ vāpy{ }aśucīny{ }api||</TEXT>
        <APP>\vc <LEM>ghrāṇā</LEM> \msCa; ghrāṇo \Ed</APP>

<TEXT> unmanas{ }tava me khyātaṃ sarvadvaitavināśanam|</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>unmanas{ }tava me</LEM> \Ed; ×××××× \msCa</APP>

<TEXT> bhavapāragasuvyaktaṃ niṣkalaṃ śivam{ }avyayam||</TEXT>
% for all sects?

<TEXT> sa śivaḥ sa paro brahmā sa viṣṇuḥ sa paro 'kṣaraḥ|</TEXT>

<TEXT> sa sūkṣmaḥ sa paro haṃsaḥ so 'kṣaraḥ kṣaravarjitaḥ||</TEXT>

% unmana for unmanaṃ or unmanas? stem form? or nom.?
<TEXT> eṣa unmana jānīhi śivaś{ }ca dvijapuṅgava|</TEXT>

<TEXT> kīrtito 'smi samāsena kim{ }anyat{ }paripṛcchasi||</TEXT>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>paripṛcchasi</LEM> \Ed; pa<UNCL>ri</UNCL>××× \msCa</APP>


<TEXT> <COLOPHON>iti vṛṣasārasaṃgrahe pañcaviṃśatitattvanirṇayo nāma viṃśatimo 'dhyāyaḥ</COLOPHON></TEXT>
        <APP> ŁColophon: $  <LEM>viṃśatimo</LEM> \msCa; viṃśatitamo \Ed</APP>

        <!-- <TR>Bravo self-control, bravo tranquillity! Bravo sacrifice, bravo penance!</TR> -->

                <!-- <TR>Or rather [you must be] Lord Viṣṇu, who has come to test me.</TR> -->

MBh 12
SECTION CCCXXXIX

"Bhishma said, 'Arrived at the spacious realm called White Island, the illustrious Rishi beheld those same white men possessed of lunar splendour (of whom I have already spoken to thee). Worshipped by them, the Rishi worshipped them in return by bending his head and reverencing them in his mind. 1 Desirous of beholding Narayana, he began to reside there, attentively engaged in the silent recitation of mantras, sacred to him, and observant of vows of the most difficult kind, with concentrated mind, the regenerate Rishi, with arms upraised, stood in Yoga, and then sang the following hymn unto the Lord of the universe, Him, viz., who is at once the soul of attributes and divested of all attributes.

SECTION CCCXL

"Bhishma said, 'Thus hymned with names that were not known to others, the Divine Narayana having the universe for his form showed himself to the ascetic Narada. His form was somewhat purer than the moon and differed from the moon in some respects. He somewhat resembled a blazing fire in complexion. The puissant Lord was somewhat of the form of Vishti. 1 He resembled in some respects the feathers of the parrot, and in some a mass of pure crystal.

<TEXT> japo yogas{ }tapo dhyānaṃ svādhyāyaś{ }ca daśa smṛtaḥ||</TEXT> 22.16
        <!-- <TR>recitation, yoga, penance, meditation and [Vedic?] study: these are the ten [sacrifices].</TR> -->
<APP>\vc <LEM>yogas{ }tapo dhyānaṃ</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNb\msNc\Ed; yoga××<UNCL>dhānaṃ</UNCL> \msNa,                                                yoga \gap\gap\ pānaṃ \msL</APP>
<APP>\vd <LEM>svādhyāyaś{ }ca</LEM> \mssCaCbCc\msNb\msNc\Ed; <UNCL>sādhyā</UNCL>yaś{ }ca \msNa,                                                sādhutapaś{ }ca \msL</APP>
        <NOTE>The missing bit is broken off in \msNa. \msL\ seems to copy \msNa\ here directly.</NOTE> 
        % Flo Dharmasūtras 5 yajñas and their "explanations" check, see also ŚDU lists 
        % BhG chs. 3 and 4.27--28 already yoga is yajña Nirajan
        % dravyayaj~
% mahāyajña in Manu, ŚDhU(?) 1 and 3
Kenji in his article:
According to the classical formulation, the five mahāyajñas are bhūtayajña, manuṣyayajña, pitṛyajña, devayajña, and brahmayajña, which are defined as giving oblation to spirits, worshipping of guests, the libation for ancestors, homa sacrifice, and the learning of Veda. (cf. Śatapathabrāhmaṇa 11.5.6.1–3, Mānavadharmaśāstra 3.68–70). We can observe that ŚDh-UMS 1.56 has agniyajña instead of manuṣyayajña. agniyajña can stand for Agnihotra. One could also argue that manuṣyatā in pāda d is somehow intended as a reference to manuṣyayajña. Mānavadharmaśāstra 4.21 has slightly different members of mahāyajñas: ṛṣiyajña, devayajña, bhūtayajña, nṛyajña, pitṛyajña replacing brahmayajña with ṛṣiyajña.

White Yajurveda:
9.33 
Sentence: a    mitro návākṣareṇa trivŕ̥tam̐ stómam úd ajayat tám új jeṣam \
Sentence: b    varuṇo dáśākṣareṇa virā́jam úd ajayat tā́m új jeṣam \
Sentence: c    índra ekā́daśākṣareṇa triṣṭúbʰam úd ajayat tā́m új jeṣam \
Sentence: d    víśve devā́ dvā́daśākṣareṇa jágatīm úd ajayam̐s tā́m új jeṣam \\

daśākṣareṇa mantreṇa ye pibanti jalaṃ narāḥ  // RKV_49.38 //
Śāradatilaka:
humādir eṣaḥ kathito rāmamantro daśākṣaraḥ || 101 ||

<SUBCHAPTER>daśākṣaramantraḥ</SUBCHAPTER>
<TEXT> daśākṣaramahārāja yogīndrasya mahātmanaḥ|</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.668
% \msCa\ 462.jpg line 4
% \msNa\ 234.jpg upper line 4
<TEXT> kathayāmi samāsena śṛṇuṣvāvahito bhava||</TEXT>
%      OṂ OṂ OṂ
% abhigamya ca yat pūrvaṃ japati tat pratyāhārārthaṃ japyam oṃ oṃ oṃ  // PSBh_1.8:2
<TEXT> praṇavādisvarā trīṇi dīrghabindusamāyutam|</TEXT>

%         Ñ? or JHA?          Y-
<TEXT> pañca pañca cavarge tu vāyubījam{ }adhasthitam||</TEXT>
% pañcamaṃ ca cavarge tu?
%  adhaḥsthitam \msCb; adha<UNCL>ḥsthitam</UNCL> \msCa, CHECK \msNa
% unmetr (two short)
%       -O
<TEXT> trayodaśasvarāyuktaṃ pañcama parikīrtitam|</TEXT>
%              ×yodaśa \msCa            pañcame \msCa\msCb\msNa
%      JHA               
<TEXT> pañcaviṃśatimaḥ ṣaṣṭha akṣaraḥ parikīrtitaḥ||</TEXT>
%                      ṣaṣṭhaḥ \msCa\msCb\msNa
%       Y-
<TEXT> yādṛśaṃ pañcamaḥ proktaṃ saptame ca prayojayet|</TEXT>
%  pañcameḥ \msCa              pañcame \msCb\msNa
%      -Ā
<TEXT> akārasvarasaṃyuktaṃ sarvapātakanāśanam||</TEXT>
%      ākāra \msCa\msNa
%                               PI
<TEXT> prathamaṃ pañcame varge tṛtīyasvarayojitam|</TEXT>
%     KṢĪ?? or HĀ (ākāra) or HĪ 
<TEXT> uktarekārasaṃyuktaṃ navamaṃ parikīrtitam||</TEXT>
% uttare \msCa\msCa\msNa         kā××××××××rikīrtitam \msCa
%      OṂ
% OṂ OṂ OṂ JHA YO   JHA YĀ PI KṢĪ OṂ
<TEXT> daśamaḥ punar{ }oṃkāraḥ mantraśreṣṭho daśākṣaraḥ|</TEXT>

<TEXT> japato dhyāyate vāpi pārthivādi krameṇa tu||</TEXT>

<TEXT> nityaṃ namraśirodvijātiguruṣu śuśrūṣaṇaṃ daivatam</TEXT>
<TEXT> tiṣṭhenācamanena cāśanakaraṃ vāmāsthimānādaram|</TEXT>
% unmetr
<TEXT> sūryāgniśaśibandhur{ }āryapurataḥ kuryān{ }na cāvaśyakam</TEXT>
<TEXT> śasye bhasmani govrajedvijajalaṃ kuryān{ }na cārkaṃ naraḥ||</TEXT>

<TEXT> pādenāgnijalaṃ spṛśen{ }na ca guruṃ pādena pādaṃ tathā</TEXT>
<TEXT> śaucaṃ kārya jalādinā ca niyataṃ nādho jalaṃ kārayet|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kuryān{ }nityabhivādanaṃ dvijaguror{ }mātāpitṛr{ }daivatam</TEXT>
<TEXT> etācāravidhiḥ samāsaniyamas{ }tubhyaṃ mayā kīrtitam||</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.669


<SUBCHAPTER>striyaḥ</SUBCHAPTER>
<ANUSTUBH/>
<TEXT> janamejaya uvāca|*</TEXT>
<NOTANUSTUBH/> śārdūlavikrīḍita 
%       -  -   -  . . -  . - . . . -? -  - . -   -  . -
<TEXT> strīṇāṃ kiṃ priyam{ }asti tad{ }vada vibho saṃsārasārastriyām</TEXT>
<TEXT> kiṃ sadbhāva na vedmi tasya viṣaye kiṃ dveṣya kiṃ tātpriyam|</TEXT>
%      -   - -?
<TEXT> paśyāmi na ca tasya garbhakalayā prāpnoti niḥsaṃśayam</TEXT>
<TEXT> māyājālasahasragāpi yuvatī kurvanti bhartā priyam||</TEXT>

<ANUSTUBH/>
<TEXT> vaiśampāyana uvāca|*</TEXT>
<NOTANUSTUBH/> śārdūlavikrīḍita 
%       -  -    -    . .    -  . -   . . . -   -  - .  -  -    .  -
<TEXT> rājan{ }kiṃ priyam{ }asti arthaparataḥ paśyāmi nānyan{ }nṛpe</TEXT>
%       -  -   -  .  . - .  -  . . . -    - -  .  -  - .  -
%      licence    .pr !
<TEXT> putrārthaikaprayojanaṃ yuvatayaḥ svāyambhuvoktāmaraiḥ|</TEXT>
% unmetr
<TEXT> kāntā nityakalā pravartanakarī dharmasakhāyā satī</TEXT>
<TEXT> māyā vāpi karoti sadya manujātyaktānya vā sevate||</TEXT>

<TEXT> strīsaṅgaṃ parivarjayen{ }narapate āyāsadaṃ duḥkhadam</TEXT>
%                                    !
% unmetr
<TEXT> mṛtyudvārabhayākaraṃ viṣagṛham{ }āpat{ }sughorālayam|</TEXT>
%                                  !
<TEXT> agnir{ }mārutamattavāraṇasama tasyānugāmī sadā</TEXT>
%                                     !
<TEXT> strīhetor{ }hatarāvaṇas{ }tridaśapa indro 'pi visthāpitaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> strīhetor{ }api candramāstribhuvane dhiktāṃ gataś{ }cāmaro|</TEXT>
<TEXT> daṇḍakṣo hatarāṣṭrapaurasahitaḥ kiṃ bhūya vakṣyāmy{ }aham||</TEXT>




<SUBCHAPTER>vipramunibhikṣunirgranthiparivrājakarṣyādayaḥ</SUBCHAPTER>
<ANUSTUBH/>
<TEXT> janamejaya uvāca|*</TEXT>

<NOTANUSTUBH/> śārdūlavikrīḍita 
%       -  -  - . . -  . -    . . .  -   - -     . -     -  . -
<TEXT> vipre kīdṛśalakṣaṇaṃ bhavati bho kīdṛg{ }muniś{ }cocyate</TEXT>
% vipro \Ed
<TEXT> tenārthena bhaveta bhikṣu bhagavan{ }nigranthi ko vā dvija|</TEXT>
% kenā \Ed 
% bhikṣurbhagavān \msCa unmetr
% nighnanti \Ed

<TEXT> kenārthena bhaved{ }dvijendra bhagavan{ }jñeyaḥ parivrājakaḥ</TEXT>
% bhagavān \Ed
% unmetrical
%                               licence
%          - -   -! . . -  . -    . . .  -   - -     . -     -  . -
<TEXT> ! jñeyāḥ kim{ }ṛṣayaś{ }ca lakṣaṇa muner{ }icchāmi jñātuṃ punaḥ||</TEXT>

<ANUSTUBH/>
<TEXT> vaiśampāyana uvāca|*</TEXT>

<NOTANUSTUBH/> śārdūlavikrīḍita 
%       -  -    -    . .    -  . -   . . . -   -  - .  -  -    .  -
<TEXT> satyaṃ śaucam{ }ahiṃsatā damaśamau bhūtānukampī sadā</TEXT>
<TEXT> ātmārāmajito svadharmanirataḥ sattvastha nityaṃ manaḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kāmakrodhayamasvadāranirataḥ saṃtyajya lobhaḥ śanaiḥ</TEXT>
<TEXT> evaṃ yaḥ kurute dvijātisuvaraḥ śūdro 'pi yaḥ saṃyamī||</TEXT>

% PARIVRĀJAKA
<TEXT> tasmāc{ }chadmakavarjitaḥ sa bhagavān{ }saṃsārabhībhidyakaḥ</TEXT>
<TEXT> yat{ }tat{ }sthānaparaṃ vrajanti puruṣāḥ tasmāt{ }parivrājakaḥ|</TEXT>

% NIRGRANTHI
%            !
<TEXT> granthidārasutaṃ dhanaṃś{ }ca virati nirgranthika socyate</TEXT>
%ṚṢI
<TEXT> ramyante ṛṣir{ }āśrame dhṛtimanas{ }tasmād{ }ṛṣiḥ socyate||</TEXT>
%Naraharinatha p.670
%DAṆḌIKA (= saṃnyāsin?)
<TEXT> kāyavāṅmanadaṇḍatatparataras{ }te daṇḍikarūcyate</TEXT>
% licence only second śra!!!
<TEXT> saddharmaśravaṇaṃ vadanti śravaṇaḥ saddharmabrahmākṣaraḥ|</TEXT>
% PĀŚUPATAS!
<TEXT> pāśaprakṣipataṃ paśutvasakalaṃ pāśūpatās{ }te smṛtāḥ</TEXT>
<TEXT> vipre pāśupatādibhikṣusakalaṃ pṛṣṭo 'smy{ }ahaṃ lakṣaṇam||</TEXT>

<TEXT> sarvaṃ tat{ }kathito 'si lakṣaṇa mayā sandhiśvanirnāśanam</TEXT>
<TEXT> prajñāsaṃgrahaśītavardhanaparaṃ saṃsāranirmūlanam|</TEXT>
<TEXT>  </TEXT>
<TEXT> etaj{ }jñānaparaṃ prabodham{ }atulaṃ nityaṃ śivaṃ dhāryate||</TEXT>

             [the end of] time (kālāgni), O king of the people.</TR> -->

<SUBCHAPTER>sapta dvīpāḥ priyavratasutāś{ }ca</SUBCHAPTER>

<TEXT> sapta dvīpās{ }tato jñeyāḥ saptasāgarasaṃvṛtāḥ|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>Then one should learn about the seven islands, which 
             are surrounded by seven oceans.</TR> -->
       <NOTE>See VSS 4.12 for a reference to the myth of Priyavrata dividing the earth into seven parts,
                thus producing the seven seas and the seven islands.</NOTE>

<TEXT> priyavratasya putro 'bhūd{ }daśa rājaparākramaḥ|| </TEXT> 24.9
        <APP>\vo <LEM>(saptaŁ...$°parākramaḥ)</LEM> \msCa\msCb; \om\ \Ed</APP>

        <NOTE>Note putro for plural. Perhaps the original read putrābhūd (with double sandhi)?</NOTE>
        <PARAL>ŁFor a similar enumeration of Priyavrata's ten sons and the seven islands,
                see, e.g., Vāyupurāṇa 33.1 ff.$</PARAL>

<TEXT> agnīdhraś{ }cāgnibāhuś{ }ca medhā medhātithir{ }vasuḥ|</TEXT>

        <!-- <TR>On the island of Puṣkara, there is a mountain called Mānasottara.</TR> -->

<TEXT> mahāvītaḥ smṛto varṣo dhātakī ca narādhipa|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vo <LEM>(mahāvītaḥŁ...$smṛtaḥ)</LEM> \msCa\msCb; \om\ \Ed</APP>

<TEXT> tasya bāhyaḥ samudro 'bhūt{ }svādūdaka iti smṛtaḥ||</TEXT> 24.16
        <APP>\vc <LEM>bāhyaḥ</LEM> \msCa\Ed; bāhya \msCb</APP>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>°dūdaka</LEM> \msCa\Ed; °dūka \msCb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Outside of [Puṣkaradvīpa], an ocean called Sweet-water (svādudaka) emerged.</TR> -->

<TEXT> catuḥṣaṣṭi smṛto lakṣo yojanānāṃ narādhipa|</TEXT>
<APP>\va <LEM>catuḥ°</LEM> \msCb; catu° \msCa</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>lakṣo</LEM> \msCa; lakṣā \msCb, \om\ \Ed</APP>

% CHECK \msCb
<TEXT> śivakṣemo dhruvaś{ }caiva sapta medhātitheḥ sutāḥ||</TEXT> 24.27
        <APP>\vc <LEM>śiva°</LEM> \msCa; śivaśiva° \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Śiva, Kṣema and Dhruva: these are Medhātithi's seven sons 
             [and the names of their countries].</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Purāṇic Encyclopedia p. 499
        ( https://www.sanskrit-lexicon.uni-koeln.de/scans/PEScan/2020/web/webtc/servepdf.php?page=499-b ):
                                ``MEDHĀTITHI I . Grandson of Svāyambhuva Manu.
                                Svāyambhuva Manu had two sons named Priyavrata and
                                Uttānapāda. Of these Priyavrata married Sarūpā and
                                Barhiṣmatī, daughters of Viśvakarmaprajāpati. Medhā-
                                tithi was the son born to Priyavrata of Sarūpā. Agnī-
                                dhra, and others were the brothers of Medhātithi.
                                Medhātithi became the King of Plakṣadvīpa after the
                                death of Priyavrata. (8th Skandha, Devī Bhāgavata).
                                Medhātithi got seven sons named Śāntahaya, Śiśira,
                                Sukhodaya, Ānanda, Śiva. Kṣemaka and Dhruva. They
                                all became Kings of Plakṣadvīpa. The countries they
                                ruled were named after them as Śāntahayavarṣa, Śiśira-
                                varṣa, Sukhodayavarṣa, Ānandavarṣa, Śivavarṣa, Kṣema-
                                kavarṣa and Dhruvavarṣa. There are seven mountains
                                showing the boundaries of these states and they are
                                called Gomeda, Cāndra, Nārada, Dundubhi, Somaka,
                                Sumana and Vaibhrāja. In these beautiful countries
                                and grand mountains live a great many Devas,
                                Gandharvas and virtuous men. (Chapter 4, Aṃśa 2,
                                Viṣṇu Purāṇa).''</NOTE>

<SUBCHAPTER>śivalokaḥ</SUBCHAPTER>
<TEXT> tasmāt{ }pareṇa bodhavyaṃ divyadhyānapuraṃ mahat|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>Beyond that, the great city of divine visions is to be recognized as</TR> -->

%                       vaiḍūrya?
<TEXT> sahasrabhaumaprāsādaṃ vaidūryamaṇitoraṇam||</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>a thousand-story palace with gates [decorated] with cat's-eye gems and</TR> -->

<TEXT> nānāratnavicitrāṇi nānābhūtagaṇākulam|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>coloured with different kinds of precious stones, inhabited by
                        different troops of beings.</TR> -->
<TEXT> sarvakāmasamṛddhāni pūrṇaṃ tatra manoharaiḥ||</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>That place is full of charming riches of all desires.</TR> -->
        <NOTE>Note samṛddhāni as a plural instrumental.</NOTE>

<TEXT> tatra siṃhāsane divye sarvaratnavibhūṣite|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>There, on a divine throne which is ornamented with all
                kinds of precious stones,</TR> -->
<TEXT> tatrāste bhagavān{ }rudraḥ somāṅkitajaṭādharaḥ||</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>the Lord Rudra is sitting, the one who wears his matted hair
             marked with the Moon,</TR> -->
<TEXT> tryakṣatribhuvanaśreṣṭhas{ }triśūlī tridaśādhipaḥ|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>the one with three eyes, the best of the three worlds,
                holding a trident, the ruler of the thirty [gods],</TR> -->

<TEXT> devyā saha mahābhāgo gaṇaiś{ }ca parivāritaḥ||</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>together with Devī, he the illustrious one, surrounded by 
                                the Gaṇas,</TR> -->
        
<TEXT> skandanandipurogaś{ }ca gaṇakoṭiśatākulaḥ|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>with Skanda and Nandi standing in front, in the crowd of
                      a hundred lakhs of Gaṇas,</TR> -->

<TEXT> anekarudrakanyābhi rūpiṇībhir{ }alaṅkitaḥ||</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>embellished CHECK with many beautiful Rudra girls.</TR> -->
        <APP>\vc <LEM>°kanyābhi°</LEM> \corr; °kanyabhi° \Ed</APP>

<TEXT> tatra puṇyanadī sapta sarvapāpāpanodanī|</TEXT>
<TEXT> suvarṇavālukādivyā ratnapāṣāṇaśobhitā||</TEXT>
% \msCa\ 472.jpg
<TEXT> pāvanī ca vareṇyā ca varārhāvaradā varā|</TEXT>
<TEXT> vareśāvarabhadrā ca suprasannā jalāśivā||</TEXT>
<TEXT> anekakusumārāmā ratnapuṣpaphaladrumāḥ|</TEXT>
% could be licence, otherwise ma-vipulā
<TEXT> anekaratnaprākārā yojanāyutam{ }ucchritāḥ||</TEXT>
<TEXT> ahiṃsāsatyaniratāḥ kāmakrodhavivarjitāḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> dhyānayogaratānityaṃ tatra modanti te narāḥ|| </TEXT>
<TEXT> tatra gomātaras sarvā nivasanti yatavratāḥ|</TEXT>
<TEXT> golokaḥ śivalokaś{ }ca eka eva vidhīyate||</TEXT>
<TEXT> tasmād{ }ūrdhaṃ paraṃ jñeyaṃ sthānatrayam{ }anuttamam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> kandagaurī maheśānaṃ nityaśuddhaṃ paraṃ śivam||</TEXT>
<TEXT> dinakṛt{ }koṭisaṅkāsam{ }anopamyaṃ sanātanam|</TEXT>
<TEXT> ādityāda ! śivāntaś{ }ca dvistheṇordhvakramaiḥ mṛstaḥ (smṛtaḥ)||</TEXT>



<SUBCHAPTER>śāstravarṇanā</SUBCHAPTER>

<TEXT> abhyantare tat{ }kathito 'dya sāraṃ</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>abhyantare tat{ }ka°</LEM> \msCa\msCb; atyantaretka° \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>Now the essence has been taught with respect to the 
             inner part[?].</TR> -->

% stem form
<TEXT> kim{ }anya rājan kathayāmi sāram|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>kim{ }anya rā°</LEM> \msCa\Ed; kim{ }anyad{ }rā° \msCb</APP>
        <!-- <TR>What other essence shall I teach, O king?</TR> -->

% stem form?
<TEXT> jñānārṇavaṃ kīrtita dharmasāram</TEXT>
<APP>\vc <LEM>jñānārṇavaṃ kīrtita dharmasāram</LEM> \msCb\Ed;                jñānārṇṇa<UNCL>ṅkīrti</UNCL>××××× \msCa</APP>
                <!-- <TR>The essence of Dharma, the ocean of knowledge, has been taught,</TR> -->

<TEXT> purāṇavedopaniṣatsusāram||</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>the very essence of the Purāṇas, the Vedas, and the Upaniṣads.</TR> -->


<TEXT> yathā hi rājā parivāramadhye</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>°vāramadhye</LEM> \msCa; °vāraṇai \msCb, °cāramadhye \Ed</APP>
                <!-- <TR>For as in a family, ...  </TR> -->

<TEXT> yathāntavartī bahivartin{ }eva|</TEXT>
<APP>\vb <LEM>yathāntava°</LEM> \msCb\Ed; yathāntarvva \msCa</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>°vartin{ }eva</LEM> \msCb\Ed; vartti<UNCL>ne</UNCL>va \msCa</APP>
                <!-- <TR>[there are those] dwelling inside and outside.</TR> -->

% stem form
<TEXT> bhuñjanti bhogān{ }satatāntavartī</TEXT>
<APP>\vc <LEM>bhuñjanti bhogān</LEM> \msCb\Ed; <UNCL>bhuñja</UNCL> ××× \msCa</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>satatāntavartī</LEM> \msCa\Ed; satatānnavartī \msCb</APP>
                <!-- <TR>Those who dwell inside enjoy themselves all the time,</TR> -->

<TEXT> kleśādhikaṃ nitya bahiḥsthitānām||</TEXT>
        <APP>\vd <LEM>bahiḥ°</LEM> \msCa\Ed; bahi° \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>and for the outsiders, [there is always just] an abundance of pain.</TR> -->


% unmetrical?
<TEXT> yathaiva rājā kariṇo 'ntadantam</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>kariṇo 'ntadantam</LEM> \msCb; kariṇo 'ntardantam \msCa, kariṇāntadantadattam \Ed</APP>
                <!-- <TR>Just like the inner teeth of an elephant, O king,</TR> -->

<TEXT> bhuñjanti bhogān{ }satataṃ narendra|</TEXT>
        <APP>\vb <LEM>bhuñjanti</LEM> \msCb\Ed; bhujanti \msCa</APP>
                <!-- <TR>enjoys the food all the time, O king,</TR> -->

%Naraharinatha p.678
% unmetrical?
<TEXT> yudhyeta rājā bahirdantabhogair</TEXT>
<APP>\vc <LEM>rājā</LEM> \msCa\Ed; rāja \msCb</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>bahirdantabhogair</LEM> \msCa\msCb; bahidattabhogair \Ed</APP>
        <!-- <TR>a ruler will fight for[?] the possession (bhoga) of [the elephant's]
                outer teeth [i.e. the tusk],</TR> -->

<TEXT> yadantaraṃ paśya samānajātam||</TEXT>
<APP>\vd <LEM>yadantaraṃ paśya samānajātam</LEM> \msCb; yadantare paśya samānajātam \Ed,                                 yadanta<UNCL>re</UNCL> ××××najātam \msCa</APP>
        <!-- <TR>The difference between the two, see, of a similar kind[???].</TR> -->

<TEXT> na dānatulyaṃ tv{ }abhayapradasya</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>There is nothing like donations for somebody who 
                offers freedom from danger.</TR> -->
<TEXT> na yajñatulyaṃ jita-indriyasya|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>There is nothing like sacrifices for him who
                        has conquered his senses.</TR> -->
<TEXT> na cārthatulyaṃ jitakāminaś{ }ca</TEXT>
        <APP>\vc <LEM>°kāminaś{ }ca</LEM> \Ed; kāmina×× \msCa</APP>
        <!-- <TR>There is nothing like wealth for him who
                        has conquered his senses.</TR> -->
<TEXT> na dharmatulyaṃ damakāmitasya||</TEXT>
<APP>\vd <LEM>na dharmatulyaṃ</LEM> \Ed; ××××× \msCa, \om\ \msCb</APP>
<APP>                 <LEM>damakāmitasya</LEM> \msCa; \om\ \msCb, damakāminasya \Ed</APP> 
        <!-- <TR>There is nothing like Dharma[?] for him whose
                        desires are tamed[?].</TR> -->

<TEXT> bahvantaraṃ naiva hi dharmayoś{ }ca</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>For there are no big differences between Dharma and a-Dharma.</TR> -->
<TEXT> kleśādhikaṃ bāhyaphalālpasāram|</TEXT>
<TEXT> yad{ }atra dharmaṃ phalanaiṣṭhikasya</TEXT>
        <APP>\vc <LEM>°naiṣṭhikasya</LEM> \Ed; °naiśikasya \msCb</APP>
<TEXT> na tulya koṭīśatayājināpi||</TEXT>

<TEXT> etat{ }pavitraṃ paramaṃ sadharmam</TEXT>
<TEXT> purā yathoktaṃ parameśvareṇa|</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>As this sacred and superior true [sat-?] Dharma
                was in the past taught by Parameśvara,</TR> -->

<TEXT> mayāpi tulyaṃ kathitaṃ yathāvat</TEXT>

<TEXT> purāṇavedopaniṣatsusāram||</TEXT>
        <!-- <TR>I too have taught it in the same form, as it is,
                the very essence of the Purāṇas, the Vedas and the Upaniṣads.</TR> -->

<TEXT> sadojasaubhāgyam{ }atīva medhā</TEXT>
        <APP>\va <LEM>sadoja°</LEM> \Ed; sadojaḥ \msCb</APP>
